Analysis

Generated by Claude Code (claude-opus-4-6) on 2026-06-24 22:00:00+00:00 from 7 judge scores across 5 cases, plus execution metadata (128 min, $66.63, 780 turns, exit 0). Recommendation leads; failure patterns, root causes, and regressions follow as supporting evidence.

Recommendation

5 of 7 judges pass thresholds. The v2 run shows significant improvement over v1: case-004 now completes (was stuck at 275 turns), JAVA_HOME enables real test execution, and the broader write permissions eliminate sandbox denial cascades. Two remaining failures are both on case-003 (log4j1→log4j2), where the pipeline produced 42 high-quality rules but exhausted its 205-turn budget before writing test data files or generating the final report. The LLM judges scored case-003's extraction and rule quality at 5/5 — the highest of any case. Fix the pipeline completion issue for case-003 (likely needs a higher turn limit for complex guides) and case-001's patterns_quality threshold (9 patterns vs 10 expected — the guide is thin).

Top actions:

  1. Raise max_turns to 300+ or investigate why case-003's test-gen sub-agents consumed so many turns for 42 rules
  2. Lower expected_min_rules for case-001 (httpclient4→5 guide is a best-practices doc, not a comprehensive migration guide — 9 patterns is reasonable)
  3. Address score.py detect_regressions TypeError crash (NoneType pass_rate for judges that return numeric scores)

Failure Patterns

Case-003: Pipeline incomplete (report_exists, test_coverage)

The log4j1→log4j2 pipeline produced 42 rules from 42 patterns with 5/5 on both LLM judges — the best extraction quality of any case. However, it consumed 205 turns and $27.10, hitting the effective capacity limit before the test-gen sub-agents could write Java source files into tests/data/. The scaffold step completed (creating the directory structure and manifest), but the test data population and report generation never finished.

Root cause: The guide has 18 content sections producing 42 rules across 9 test groups. The pipeline needed to construct regex fix (invalid Go negative lookahead → re-merge → re-construct), which consumed extra turns. By the time test-gen started, there wasn't enough budget for 2 parallel agents to write 42 test data files.

Case-001: Thin guide (patterns_quality partial)

The httpclient4→5 migration guide is a best-practices document, not a comprehensive API migration reference. 9 patterns were extracted (5 with unqualified FQNs that were dropped during construct). The expected_min_rules: 10 annotation is too high for this guide's content. The LLM extraction judge gave 4/5, confirming ~90% of available artifacts were captured.

Root Causes

  1. Turn/budget exhaustion on complex guides: Case-003's 42 rules require proportionally more test-gen work than simpler cases. The regex fix retry (negative lookahead → Go-compatible alternative) consumed ~5 extra minutes. Combined with 9 test groups and 42 rules, the pipeline ran out of capacity.
  1. Annotation calibration: Case-001's expected_min_rules: 10 doesn't match the actual guide content. This is a dataset annotation issue, not a skill issue.
  1. Score.py infrastructure bug: detect_regressions crashes with TypeError: '<' not supported between instances of 'NoneType' and 'float' when pass_rate is None (happens for judges that return numeric scores like 0.5 instead of boolean). This is a harness bug — the summary.yaml is written before the crash, so scoring data is preserved but the HTML report generation fails.

Per-Case Details

case-001-httpclient4-to-httpclient5 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $5.95 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The patterns.json captured ~90% of meaningful migration artifacts from the guide: package relocation (org.apache.http), getStatusLine() removal, SSLConnectionSocketFactory changes, timeout parameter changes (setConnectTimeout, setSocketTimeout, setSoTimeout), setConnectionTimeToLive behavioral change, setSSLSocketFactory removal, and EntityTemplate constructor changes. Minor gaps include HttpClientContext configuration changes and explicit HttpEntity/response content handling patterns. The main limitation was that 5 of 9 patterns had non-FQN source_fqn values, preventing them from becoming rules, but from an extraction standpoint the artifacts were identified. The guide itself is more of a best-practices document than a comprehensive migration guide, which limits the total artifact count.

patterns_quality0.5

9 patterns extracted, expected at least 10

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 4 rules, 100% pass rate

rule_correctness4

Rules reviewed: All 4 generated rules (http-client-import-00010, http-client-method-00010, http-client-method-00020, ssl-method-00010) plus the 9 patterns that fed them.

When condition accuracy: All 4 rules correctly match source-side (HttpClient 4.x) artifacts:

  • org.apache.http PACKAGE match is correct for the broad import rule
  • org.apache.http.HttpResponse.getStatusLine METHOD_CALL correctly targets the 4.x API
  • org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate CONSTRUCTOR_CALL correctly targets the 4.x class
  • org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory CONSTRUCTOR_CALL correctly targets the 4.x class

All verified against actual 4.x JARs (4 verified in verify-results.json). No target-side patterns used in when conditions.

Message quality: All rules include clear before/after code examples with proper imports, explain what changed and how to migrate, and include additional info bullet points. The messages are detailed and actionable. The http-client-import-00010 rule has a particularly comprehensive mapping table, though it has a minor formatting issue with duplicate \"Specific replacements\" headers.

Documentation URL: All rules link to https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html — this is the specific migration guide page, not just the homepage. It's the same URL for all rules, which is appropriate since the guide covers all these changes.

Category and effort: All rules are marked mandatory which is correct — these are breaking API changes. Effort is 5 for most rules and 7 for the SSL rule, which seems reasonable given SSL/TLS configuration requires more restructuring.

No hallucinations: All source-side classes/methods are real and verified. The target-side replacements (org.apache.hc.client5., org.apache.hc.core5.) are accurate for HttpClient 5.x.

Coverage gaps: 5 of 9 patterns were dropped because source_fqn was not fully qualified (e.g., bare setConnectTimeout instead of org.apache.http.client.config.RequestConfig.Builder.setConnectTimeout). This is a significant loss — timeout and TTL configuration changes are important migration concerns. Only 4 rules were ultimately produced from 9 patterns, meaning ~55% of identified patterns were lost.

Minor issues:

  • Duplicate \"Specific replacements\" section headers in http-client-import-00010
  • The 5 skipped patterns represent real, important migration concerns that should have had proper FQNs
  • All tests pass (100% pass rate), confirming rule correctness
  • The guide.md preparation steps still reference 4.x API patterns (e.g., setConnectTimeout(60000)) which is appropriate for context but the code samples mix 4.x and 5.x conventions somewhat confusingly

output/httpclient4-to-httpclient5-20260624-111418/tests/data/ssl/src/main/java/com/example/Application.java
package com.example;

// Rule: ssl-method-00010
import org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory;
import org.apache.http.ssl.SSLContexts;
import org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient;
import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;

import javax.net.ssl.SSLContext;

public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        // Rule: ssl-method-00010
        SSLContext sslContext = SSLContexts.createSystemDefault();
        SSLConnectionSocketFactory sslFactory = new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(
                sslContext,
                new String[] { "TLSv1.2" },
                null,
                SSLConnectionSocketFactory.getDefaultHostnameVerifier());

        CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
                .setSSLSocketFactory(sslFactory)
                .build();
    }
}
output/httpclient4-to-httpclient5-20260624-111418/tests/data/http-client/src/main/java/com/example/Application.java
package com.example;

// Rule: http-client-import-00010
import org.apache.http.HttpEntity;
import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpGet;
import org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient;
import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;
import org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate;
import org.apache.http.entity.ContentType;

import java.io.IOException;
import java.io.OutputStream;

public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        // Rule: http-client-import-00010
        CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.createDefault();
        HttpGet request = new HttpGet("http://example.com");

        // Rule: http-client-method-00010
        HttpResponse response = client.execute(request);
        int statusCode = response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode();

        // Rule: http-client-method-00020
        EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(new org.apache.http.entity.ContentProducer() {
            @Override
            public void writeTo(OutputStream outstream) throws IOException {
                outstream.write("test".getBytes());
                outstream.flush();
            }
        });
    }
}

Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. A permission denial means the action is blocked, not that the syntax was wrong. Move to the next pipeline step or end the pipeline.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` first (use the pipeline timestamp to avoid collisions when multiple invocations run in parallel), read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

output/httpclient4-to-httpclient5-20260624-111418/guide.md
# Migration from Apache HttpClient 4.x APIs

It is strongly encouraged to follow the best practices and common use patterns in programming with Apache HttpClient 4.x. They remain largely unchanged between 4.x and 5.x release series. Correctly written code will be easier to port to 5.x APIs and from the classic I/O model to the async I/O model.

## []()Preparation steps

01. Make sure there are no references to deprecated functions or classes
02. HttpClient uses tries to use sensible defaults but it is generally recommended to adjust SSL/TLS parameters and timeout settings for the specific application context.
03. Explicitly specify TLSv1.2 in order to disable older, less secure versions of the SSL/TLS protocol. Please note HttpClient 4.5 disables all SSL versions by default.
04. Set finite socket and connect timeouts.
05. Set a finite connection total time to live (TTL). Use a negative value for connections with unlimited / infinite time to live. Please note as of version 5.0 HttpClient treats zero TTL as an instruction that connections are not meant to be re-used.
06. Favor the `strict` cookie policy.
07. IMPORTANT: Always re-use `CloseableHttpClient` instances. They are expensive to create, but they are also fully thread safe, so multiple threads can use the same instance of `CloseableHttpClient` to execute multiple requests concurrently taking full advantage of persistent connection re-use and connection pooling.
    
    ```java
    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
            .setSSLSocketFactory(new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(
                    SSLContexts.createSystemDefault(),
                    new String[] { "TLSv1.2" },
                    null,
                    SSLConnectionSocketFactory.getDefaultHostnameVerifier()))
            .setConnectionTimeToLive(1, TimeUnit.MINUTES)
            .setDefaultSocketConfig(SocketConfig.custom()
                    .setSoTimeout(60000)
                    .build())
            .setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
                    .setConnectTimeout(60000)
                    .setSocketTimeout(60000)
                    .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
                    .build())
            .build();
    ```
08. Cookie store and credentials providers can be shared by multiple execution threads. They can still be shared by multiple message exchnages without being set at `CloseableHttpClient` construction time.
    
    ```java
    CookieStore cookieStore = new BasicCookieStore();
    CredentialsProvider credentialsProvider = new BasicCredentialsProvider();
    ```
09. While `CloseableHttpClient` should have the default configuration applicable to all all messages exchanges one can use `HttpContext` to customize individual request execution parameters.
    
    ```java
    HttpClientContext clientContext = HttpClientContext.create();
    clientContext.setCookieStore(cookieStore);
    clientContext.setCredentialsProvider(credentialsProvider);
    clientContext.setRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
            .setConnectTimeout(60000)
            .setSocketTimeout(60000)
            .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
            .build());
    ```
10. Always set content type and content encoding on the entity and let HttpClient generate request headers automatically.
    
    ```java
    JsonFactory jsonFactory = new JsonFactory();
    ObjectMapper objectMapper = new ObjectMapper(jsonFactory);
    
    HttpPost httpPost = new HttpPost("https://httpbin.org/post");
    List<NameValuePair> requestData = Arrays.asList(
            new BasicNameValuePair("name1", "value1"),
            new BasicNameValuePair("name2", "value2"));
    
    EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(outstream -> {
        objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, requestData);
        outstream.flush();
    
    });
    requestEntity.setContentType(ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON.toString());
    httpPost.setEntity(requestEntity);
    ```
11. Consume response content directly from the content stream and convert it to a higher level object without converting it to an intermediate string or byte array.
12. Favor HTTP response handlers for response processing, thus making connection release automatic.
    
    ```java
    JsonNode responseData = client.execute(httpPost, response -> {
        if (response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode() >= 300) {
            throw new ClientProtocolException(Objects.toString(response.getStatusLine()));
        }
        final HttpEntity responseEntity = response.getEntity();
        if (responseEntity == null) {
            return null;
        }
        try (InputStream inputStream = responseEntity.getContent()) {
            return objectMapper.readTree(inputStream);
        }
    });
    System.out.println(responseData);
    ```
13. `CloseableHttpClient` instances should be closed when no longer needed or about to go out of scope.
    
    ```java
    client.close();
    ```

- ruleID: http-client-import-00010
  description: org.apache.http package relocated to org.apache.hc.client5 and org.apache.hc.core5 in HttpClient 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient4
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient5
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |
    The `org.apache.http` package has been completely restructured in Apache HttpClient 5.x. All classes under `org.apache.http` have been moved to either `org.apache.hc.client5.http` (client classes) or `org.apache.hc.core5.http` (core classes).

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.HttpEntity;
    import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
    import org.apache.http.client.HttpClient;
    import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpGet;
    import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpPost;
    import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;
    import org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.HttpEntity;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.methods.HttpGet;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.methods.HttpPost;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.HttpClients;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.CloseableHttpClient;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.CloseableHttpResponse;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Client-side classes (HttpClient, HttpGet, HttpPost, etc.) moved to `org.apache.hc.client5.http`
    - Core classes (HttpEntity, HttpResponse, etc.) moved to `org.apache.hc.core5.http`
    - Some classes were renamed (e.g., `HttpResponse` became `ClassicHttpResponse`)
    - Import statements must be updated for every class from the `org.apache.http` namespace
    - See the Apache HttpClient 5.x migration guide for full class mapping

    ### Specific replacements

    | Old class | Replacement |
    |---|---|
    | `org.apache.http.client.ClientProtocolException` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.ClientProtocolException |


    ### Specific replacements

    | Old class | Replacement |
    |---|---|
    | `org.apache.http.impl.client.BasicCredentialsProvider` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.auth.BasicCredentialsProvider |
    | `org.apache.http.NameValuePair` | org.apache.hc.core5.http.NameValuePair |
    | `org.apache.http.message.BasicNameValuePair` | org.apache.hc.core5.http.message.BasicNameValuePair |
    | `org.apache.http.client.CookieStore` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.cookie.CookieStore |
    | `org.apache.http.impl.client.BasicCookieStore` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.cookie.BasicCookieStore |
    | `org.apache.http.cookie.StandardCookieSpec` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.cookie.StandardCookieSpec |
    | `org.apache.http.client.CredentialsProvider` | org.apache.hc.client5.http.auth.CredentialsProvider |
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http
        location: PACKAGE
- ruleID: http-client-method-00010
  description: getStatusLine() removed in HttpClient 5.x; use getCode() instead
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient4
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient5
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `StatusLine` class and `getStatusLine()` method have been removed in Apache HttpClient 5.x. The status code is now obtained directly via `getCode()` on the response object.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
    import org.apache.http.StatusLine;

    HttpResponse response = client.execute(request);
    int statusCode = response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode();
    String reasonPhrase = response.getStatusLine().getReasonPhrase();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.CloseableHttpResponse;

    CloseableHttpResponse response = client.execute(request);
    int statusCode = response.getCode();
    String reasonPhrase = response.getReasonPhrase();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `StatusLine` class is removed entirely in HttpClient 5.x
    - `getStatusLine().getStatusCode()` is replaced by `getCode()`
    - `getStatusLine().getReasonPhrase()` is replaced by `getReasonPhrase()`
    - The protocol version is available via `getVersion()`
    - Response handlers using `getStatusLine()` must be updated
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.HttpResponse.getStatusLine
        location: METHOD_CALL
- ruleID: http-client-method-00020
  description: EntityTemplate constructor and content type setting changed in HttpClient 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient4
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient5
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Apache HttpClient 5.x, `EntityTemplate` has been moved from `org.apache.http.entity` to `org.apache.hc.core5.http.io.entity`. The content type is now set via the constructor or abstract entity methods rather than calling `setContentType(String)` separately.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate;
    import org.apache.http.entity.ContentType;

    EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(outstream -> {
        objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, requestData);
        outstream.flush();
    });
    requestEntity.setContentType(ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON.toString());
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.io.entity.EntityTemplate;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ContentType;

    EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(
            -1, ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON, null,
            outstream -> {
                objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, requestData);
                outstream.flush();
            });
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `EntityTemplate` moved from `org.apache.http.entity` to `org.apache.hc.core5.http.io.entity`
    - The constructor now accepts content length, content type, and encoding as parameters
    - The `setContentType(String)` method is removed; use the constructor parameter instead
    - `ContentType` moved from `org.apache.http.entity` to `org.apache.hc.core5.http`
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate
        location: CONSTRUCTOR_CALL

output/httpclient4-to-httpclient5-20260624-111418/rules/ssl.yaml
- ruleID: ssl-method-00010
  description: SSLConnectionSocketFactory constructor replaced by builder pattern or TLS strategy in 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient4
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient5
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Apache HttpClient 5.x, the `SSLConnectionSocketFactory` constructor API has changed significantly. The 4.x pattern of creating an `SSLConnectionSocketFactory` with SSLContext, protocol versions, cipher suites, and hostname verifier is replaced by a builder pattern or TLS strategy configuration.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory;
    import org.apache.http.ssl.SSLContexts;

    SSLConnectionSocketFactory sslFactory = new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(
            SSLContexts.createSystemDefault(),
            new String[] { "TLSv1.2" },
            null,
            SSLConnectionSocketFactory.getDefaultHostnameVerifier());

    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
            .setSSLSocketFactory(sslFactory)
            .build();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.ssl.ClientTlsStrategyBuilder;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.ssl.SSLContexts;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ssl.TLS;

    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
            .setConnectionManager(PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
                    .setTlsSocketStrategy(ClientTlsStrategyBuilder.create()
                            .setSslContext(SSLContexts.createSystemDefault())
                            .setTlsVersions(TLS.V_1_2)
                            .build())
                    .build())
            .build();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The 4.x `SSLConnectionSocketFactory` direct constructor is replaced by `ClientTlsStrategyBuilder`
    - `setSSLSocketFactory()` on `HttpClientBuilder` is replaced by configuring TLS on the connection manager
    - TLS protocol versions are now specified via the `TLS` enum instead of string arrays
    - The hostname verifier is configured through the builder rather than as a constructor parameter
    - `SSLContexts` has moved from `org.apache.http.ssl` to `org.apache.hc.core5.ssl`
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory
        location: CONSTRUCTOR_CALL

case-002-spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $18.86 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The output demonstrates strong coverage of the migration guide's key artifacts. Let me walk through the major sections:

Well-covered areas:

  • Features removed (Undertow, Pulsar Reactive, embedded launch scripts, Spring Session Hazelcast/MongoDB, Spock) — all captured
  • Deprecated starters (OAuth2 auth server/client/resource-server, web→webmvc, web-services→webservices) — all captured
  • Core features (JSpecify nullability, BootstrapRegistry/Context/Initializer relocation, EnvironmentPostProcessor relocation, PropertyMapper API changes, DevTools LiveReload) — all captured
  • Jackson 3 migration (package rename com.fasterxml→tools.jackson, class renames JsonObjectSerializer→ObjectValueSerializer, JsonValueDeserializer→ObjectValueDeserializer, Jackson2ObjectMapperBuilderCustomizer→JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer, @JsonComponent→@JacksonComponent, @JsonMixin→@JacksonMixin, property renames spring.jackson.read/write→spring.jackson.json.read/write, spring.jackson.parser→spring.jackson.json.read) — all captured
  • Dependencies (AOP starter rename, Spring Retry removal, Spring Authorization Server version property, classic uber-jar loader, CycloneDX plugin, optional dependencies in Maven, Flyway/Liquibase starter requirements) — all captured
  • Data features (Elasticsearch Rest5Client, @EntityScan relocation, spring.dao→spring.persistence property, MongoDB property renames, MongoDB management property renames, Hibernate dependency changes) — all captured
  • Messaging (Kafka Streams customizer, Kafka retry backoff.random→jitter, AMQP retry customizers) — all captured
  • Testing (@MockBean/@SpyBean removal, MockitoTestExecutionListener, MockMvc+@SpringBootTest, TestRestTemplate, @PropertyMapping relocation, HtmlUnit attribute changes) — all captured
  • Web (fonts in static locations, HttpMessageConverters deprecation, forwarded headers strategy, Jersey+Jackson2, Tomcat WAR deployment) — all captured
  • Spring Batch in-memory default — captured

Notable gaps:

  • The massive Starters and Modules tables (60+ rows each) are not individually captured as patterns — these are reference tables, not actionable migration artifacts per se, though the guide mentions them as important
  • spring.jackson.use-jackson2-defaults property and spring.jackson2 namespace for Jackson 2 compatibility not captured
  • spring-boot-jackson2 module as a stop-gap dependency not captured as its own pattern (only mentioned in Jersey context)
  • spring.jackson.find-and-add-modules=false property change (Jackson auto-detecting all modules) not captured as a separate pattern
  • Logback default charset change (UTF-8 harmonization) not captured
  • org.springframework.lang.Nullable for actuator endpoint parameters specifically not captured (though general JSpecify migration is)
  • WebClient no longer auto-configured by @SpringBootTest (pattern exists for TestRestTemplate but WebClient specifically not called out)
  • RestTestClient as new replacement class not captured as its own pattern
  • ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer/ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer target classes mentioned but not as separate detectable patterns
  • spring.factories file updates for relocated classes not specifically captured
  • Classic starters (spring-boot-starter-classic, spring-boot-starter-test-classic) as migration aids not captured as detection patterns
  • spring.mongodb.representation.big-decimal new required property not independently captured

The coverage is comprehensive for actionable, detectable migration artifacts. Most gaps are either informational items, reference tables that aren't individually actionable, or minor properties. The 72 patterns cover the vast majority of breaking changes a developer would encounter.

patterns_qualityPASS

72 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 72 rules, 100% pass rate

rule_correctness4

Rules are overwhelmingly correct with accurate when conditions targeting source-side artifacts, clear before/after migration examples, and specific documentation URLs. Categories and effort levels are well-calibrated. One rule (jackson-import-00030 for JsonValueDeserializer) failed source verification suggesting the class may not exist exactly as named in 3.5.0, and PropertyMapping.Skip also failed verification - these represent minor accuracy concerns. The 28 kantra-limitation failures are all java.dependency rules which is a known tooling limitation, not a rule quality issue. Test pass rate for non-limitation rules is 100%.

// Rule: web-import-00010

// Rule: web-import-00020

    The liveness and readiness probes are now enabled by default in Spring Boot 4. The health endpoint now exposes the `liveness` and `readiness` groups by default.

    ### Migration Steps
    - If you explicitly set `management.endpoint.health.probes.enabled=true`, it is now redundant and can be removed
    - If you relied on probes being disabled by default, set `management.endpoint.health.probes.enabled=false` to restore the previous behavior
    - Review your health endpoint security configuration since the probes are now exposed by default
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#liveness-and-readiness-probes

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-111421/rules/build.yaml
- ruleID: build-xml-00010
  description: Embedded executable uber jar launch scripts removed in Spring Boot 4
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Support for embedded launch scripts, used to create "fully executable" jar files that can be run directly (e.g., `./myapp.jar`), has been removed from Spring Boot 4.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Remove `<executable>true</executable>` from the `spring-boot-maven-plugin` configuration in your `pom.xml`
    2. Use `java -jar myapp.jar` to run your application instead of `./myapp.jar`
    3. If you need OS-level service integration, consider using [Gradle's application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html) or systemd/init.d service wrappers

    ### Additional Info

    - You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot's build plugins and run them using `java -jar`
    - The embedded launch script feature was Unix-specific and had limitations
    - The removal aligns with [recommendations for efficient deployments](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/packaging/efficient.html)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='plugin'][*[local-name()='artifactId' and text()='spring-boot-maven-plugin']]/*[local-name()='configuration']/*[local-name()='executable' and text()='true']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml

    2. Use `java -jar myapp.jar` to run your application instead of `./myapp.jar`
    3. If you need OS-level service integration, consider using [Gradle's application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html) or systemd/init.d service wrappers

    ### Additional Info

    - You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot's build plugins and run them using `java -jar`
    - The embedded launch script feature was Unix-specific and had limitations
    - The removal aligns with [recommendations for efficient deployments](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/packaging/efficient.html)
  links:

      title: Migration Documentation

- ruleID: build-xml-00020
  description: Optional dependencies are no longer included in uber jars in Spring Boot 4
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Optional dependencies are no longer included in uber jars in Spring Boot 4. If your application relies on optional dependencies being packaged in the uber jar, you need to update your build configuration.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review your optional dependencies to determine if any need to be in the uber jar
    2. If needed, add `<includeOptional>true</includeOptional>` to the Spring Boot Maven plugin configuration:

    ```xml
    <plugin>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
        <configuration>
            <includeOptional>true</includeOptional>
        </configuration>
    </plugin>
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - This only affects Maven-based projects using the Spring Boot Maven plugin for uber jar packaging
    - Consider whether the dependency truly needs to be optional, or if it should be a required dependency
    - See [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#optional-dependencies-in-maven)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#optional-dependencies-in-maven
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: /m:project/m:dependencies/m:dependency[m:optional/text()='true']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml
- ruleID: build-xml-00030
  description: Classic uber-jar loader has been removed in Spring Boot 4
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The classic uber-jar loader has been removed from Spring Boot 4. You should remove any loader implementation configuration from your Maven build file.

    ### Before

    ```xml
    <plugin>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
        <configuration>
            <loaderImplementation>CLASSIC</loaderImplementation>
        </configuration>
    </plugin>
    ```

    ### After

    ```xml
    <plugin>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
    </plugin>
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - Simply remove the `<loaderImplementation>CLASSIC</loaderImplementation>` element from your pom.xml
    - The default loader implementation in Spring Boot 4 is the only supported option
    - See [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#classic-uber-jar-loader-support)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#classic-uber-jar-loader-support
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='loaderImplementation' and text()='CLASSIC']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml

    - The default loader implementation in Spring Boot 4 is the only supported option
    - See [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#classic-uber-jar-loader-support)
  links:

- ruleID: core-dependency-00010
  description: Spring Boot 3.x must be upgraded to 4.0; requires Java 17+, Jakarta EE 11, Servlet 6.1, and Spring Framework 7.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4.0 requires upgrading from Spring Boot 3.x. Before upgrading, ensure your project meets the system requirements.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Upgrade to the latest Spring Boot 3.5.x version first
    2. Review and remove all deprecated API calls
    3. Ensure Java 17 or later is configured
    4. Verify Kotlin v2.2+ if using Kotlin
    5. Verify GraalVM v25+ if using native-image
    6. Update to Spring Framework 7.x if managing it directly
    7. Ensure Servlet 6.1 compatible container (Jakarta EE 11)
    8. Upgrade to Spring Boot 4.0.x

    ### Additional Info

    - Spring Boot 4 is based on Jakarta EE 11 and requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline
    - Spring Framework 7.x is required; if you manage Spring Framework dependencies directly, update them
    - Review the full [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide) for all breaking changes
    - Use `spring-boot-properties-migrator` to help with configuration property changes
    - Review dependency management changes between [3.5.x](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/3.5/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) and [4.0.x](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html)
  links:

      title: Migration Documentation

- ruleID: core-import-00010
  description: Spring Framework nullable annotations replaced by JSpecify in Spring Boot 4
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |
    Spring Boot 4.0 adds JSpecify nullability annotations. If you are using a null checker in your build or using Kotlin, this could lead to compilation failures because of now nullable or non-nullable types.

    The `org.springframework.lang` package annotations (`@Nullable`, `@NonNull`, etc.) should be migrated to JSpecify annotations.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Replace imports from `org.springframework.lang` with the equivalent JSpecify annotations from `org.jspecify.annotations`
    2. Review the Spring Framework migration guide: https://docs.spring.io/spring-framework/reference/core/null-safety.html#null-safety-migrating
    3. If using Kotlin, test for compilation failures due to stricter nullability enforcement

    ### Additional Info

    - JSpecify provides more standardized null-safety annotations across the Java ecosystem
    - Kotlin users may see compilation failures where types are now non-nullable
    - Projects using null-checker tools (SpotBugs, Checker Framework) may need updated configurations
    - See [Migrating from Spring null-safety annotations](https://docs.spring.io/spring-framework/reference/core/null-safety.html#null-safety-migrating)

    ### Specific replacements

    | Old class | Replacement |
    |---|---|
    | `org.springframework.lang.Nullable` | org.jspecify.annotations.Nullable |
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#jspecify-nullability-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.lang
        location: PACKAGE

- ruleID: data-import-00010
  description: RestClientBuilderCustomizer replaced by Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer for Elasticsearch
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The auto-configuration for the deprecated low-level Elasticsearch `RestClient` has been replaced with auto-configuration for the new `Rest5Client`. If you were using `RestClientBuilderCustomizer` to customize the client, you must now use `Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.RestClientBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public RestClientBuilderCustomizer customizer() {
        return builder -> builder.setRequestConfigCallback(config -> config.setConnectTimeout(5000));
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer customizer() {
        return builder -> builder.setRequestConfigCallback(config -> config.setConnectTimeout(Timeout.ofSeconds(5)));
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `ElasticsearchClient` and `ReactiveElasticsearchClient` support remains and has been updated to use the new client
    - The `co.elastic.clients:elasticsearch-java` module now consolidates client code including sniffer support
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#elasticsearch-client
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#elasticsearch-client
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.RestClientBuilderCustomizer
        location: IMPORT

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.domain.EntityScan;

    @EntityScan(basePackages = "com.example.entities")
    public class AppConfig { }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.persistence.autoconfigure.EntityScan;

    @EntityScan(basePackages = "com.example.entities")
    public class AppConfig { }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The new `spring-boot-persistence` module houses general persistence-related code and properties
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#persistence-modules

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: Flyway auto-configuration now requires spring-boot-starter-flyway instead of direct flyway-core dependency
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4 has a new modular design. Flyway auto-configuration now requires the dedicated `spring-boot-starter-flyway` starter instead of just the direct `org.flywaydb:flyway-core` dependency.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Add `spring-boot-starter-flyway` to your POM or Gradle build file.
    2. You may remove the direct `org.flywaydb:flyway-core` dependency as it is now provided transitively by the starter.
    3. If using test infrastructure, also add `spring-boot-starter-flyway-test`.

    ### Additional Info
    - The new modular design means auto-configuration classes are no longer in a single large jar.
    - Without the starter, Flyway-related auto-configuration beans will not be registered.
    - This change affects applications that previously relied on having just `flyway-core` on the classpath.
    - Consider using `spring-boot-starter-classic` as an intermediate step if you have many such dependencies to migrate.
    - See the [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#module-dependencies) for full details.
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#module-dependencies
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.flywaydb.flyway-core
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    1. Add `spring-boot-starter-security-test` to your test dependencies.
    2. You may remove the direct `org.springframework.security:spring-security-test` dependency as it is now provided transitively by the starter.
    3. All test starter POMs bring `spring-boot-starter-test` transitively, so you don't need to define that starter separately.

    ### Additional Info
    - Without the test starter, security test annotations may silently fail or produce hard-to-diagnose errors.
    - This applies to all technologies that define their own test infrastructure -- swap to the `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test` equivalent.
    - Consider using `spring-boot-starter-test-classic` as an intermediate step during migration.
    - See the [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#test-code) for full details.
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#test-code
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.security.spring-security-test
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00040
  description: spring-boot-starter-test is now modular in Spring Boot 4; consider spring-boot-starter-test-classic for gradual migration
  category: potential
  effort: 5

  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4 has a new modular design. The base `spring-boot-starter-test` no longer includes all test auto-configuration modules transitively. If your tests rely on test infrastructure that was previously available through transitive dependencies, you may encounter missing bean or class-not-found errors.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. **Quick fix:** Replace `spring-boot-starter-test` with `spring-boot-starter-test-classic` to restore the Spring Boot 3-like test classpath.
    2. **Recommended:** Identify the specific technologies under test and add the corresponding `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test` dependencies.
    3. All test starter POMs bring `spring-boot-starter-test` transitively, so you don't need to define it separately once you have technology-specific test starters.

    ### Additional Info
    - Classic test starters provide all test modules but exclude their transitive dependencies.
    - The classic test starters are recommended as an intermediate migration step.
    - For example, if testing security features, add `spring-boot-starter-security-test` instead of direct `spring-security-test`.
    - Review the full [Starters table](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#starters) to identify which test starters your application needs.
    - See the [Migration Strategy](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#migration-strategy) for the recommended two-step approach.
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#classic-starters
      title: Migration Documentation

    ### Before

    ```xml
    </dependency>
    ```

    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-security-oauth2-authorization-server</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The old starter remains available but is deprecated.
    - This rename provides better alignment with the `spring-boot-security-oauth2-authorization-server` module.
    - Update your POM or Gradle build file to use the new artifact name.
    - See the [Deprecated Starters](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#deprecated-starters) section for all renamed starters.

- ruleID: devtools-dependency-00010
  description: DevTools Live Reload is now disabled by default in Spring Boot 4
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    DevTools Live Reload support is now disabled by default in Spring Boot 4. If you rely on live reload functionality during development, you will need to explicitly enable it.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Add `spring.devtools.livereload.enabled=true` to your `application.properties` or `application.yml` to re-enable live reload
    2. Alternatively, accept the new default if you do not use live reload

    ### Additional Info

    - This change only affects development-time behavior; production deployments are unaffected
    - The LiveReload server was previously enabled automatically when DevTools was on the classpath
    - See [Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#devtools-live-reload-support)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#devtools-live-reload-support
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-devtools
        upperbound: 4.0.0
