Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` first (use the pipeline timestamp to avoid collisions when multiple invocations run in parallel), read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",
    "is_error": false,

# Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide

[Jump to bottom](#wiki-pages-box)

Andy Wilkinson edited this page Apr 30, 2026 · [67 revisions](/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide/_history)

This document is meant to help you migrate your application to Spring Boot 4.0.

## Before You Start

[](#before-you-start)

### Upgrade to the Latest `3.5.x` Version

[](#upgrade-to-the-latest-35x-version)

Before you start the upgrade, make sure to upgrade to the latest available `3.5.x` version. This will make sure that you are building against the most recent dependencies of that line.

Please take time to review any calls you might be making to deprecated methods as these will be removed in Spring Boot 4.0.

### Review Dependencies

[](#review-dependencies)

The move to Spring Boot 4 will upgrade a number of dependencies and might require work on your end. You can review [dependency management for `3.5.x`](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/3.5/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) with [dependency management for `4.0.x`](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) to asses how your project is affected.

You may also use dependencies that are not managed by Spring Boot (e.g. [Spring Cloud](https://github.com/spring-cloud/spring-cloud-release/wiki/Supported-Versions#supported-releases)). As your project defines an explicit version for those, identify the compatible version before upgrading.

### Review System Requirements

[](#review-system-requirements)

Spring Boot 4.0 requires Java 17 or later. Using the latest LTS release of Java is encouraged.

Spring Boot applications can also be developed using Kotlin where v2.2 or later must be used.

If you’re using GraalVM’s native-image, v25 or later must be used.

Spring Boot 4 is based on Jakarta EE 11 and requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline.

If you manage dependencies directly, make sure you update them accordingly. In particular, you must use Spring Framework 7.x.

### Review Deprecations from Spring Boot 3.x

[](#review-deprecations-from-spring-boot-3x)

Classes, methods and properties that were deprecated in Spring Boot 3.x have been removed in this release. Please ensure that you aren’t calling deprecated methods before upgrading.

## Upgrade to Spring Boot 4

[](#upgrade-to-spring-boot-4)

Once you have reviewed the state of your project and its dependencies, upgrade to the latest maintenance release of Spring Boot 4.0.

### Configuration Properties Migration

[](#configuration-properties-migration)

Configuration properties were renamed/removed and developers need to update their `application.properties`/`application.yml` accordingly. To help you with that, Spring Boot provides a `spring-boot-properties-migrator` module. Once added as a dependency to your project, this will not only analyze your application’s environment and print diagnostics at startup, but also temporarily migrate properties at runtime for you.

You can add the migrator by adding the following to your Maven `pom.xml`:

```
<dependency>
	<groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
	<artifactId>spring-boot-properties-migrator</artifactId>
	<scope>runtime</scope>
</dependency>
```

Or if you use Gradle:

```
runtimeOnly("org.springframework.boot:spring-boot-properties-migrator")
```

| Note | Once you’re done with the migration, please make sure to remove this module from your project’s dependencies. |
|------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

### Features Removed From This Release

[](#features-removed-from-this-release)

The features have been removed from this release and are no longer available

#### Undertow

[](#undertow)

Spring Boot 4 requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline, with which Undertow is not yet compatible. As a result, Undertow support is dropped, including the Undertow starter and the ability to use Undertow as an embedded server.

We do not recommend deploying Spring Boot 4.0 applications to a non-Servlet 6.1 compliant container.

#### Pulsar Reactive

[](#pulsar-reactive)

Following the decision of removing reactor support in Spring Pulsar, Spring Boot no longer manages the reactive Pulsar client. Auto-configuration for Spring Pulsar Reactive has been removed as well.

#### Embedded Executable Uber Jar Launch Scripts

[](#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts)

Support for embedded launch scripts, used to create "fully executable" jar files, has been removed. The support was specific to Unix-like operating systems and had a number of limitations, most notably conflicting with the [recommendations for efficient deployments](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/packaging/efficient.html). If you still require similar functionality, we recommend looking at alternatives such as [Gradle’s application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html).

You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot’s build plugins and run them using `java -jar`.

#### Spring Session Hazelcast

[](#spring-session-hazelcast)

Spring Session Hazelcast is now under the [leadership of the Hazelcast team](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/14/spring-session-hazelcast-new-leadership). As such, direct support for Spring Session Hazelcast has been removed from Spring Boot itself.

#### Spring Session MongoDB

[](#spring-session-mongodb)

Spring Session MongoDB is now under the [leadership of the MongoDB team](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/14/spring-session-mongodb-new-leadership). As such, direct support for Spring Session MongoDB has been removed from Spring Boot itself.

#### Spock Integration

[](#spock-integration)

Spring Boot’s Spock integration has been removed as Spock does not yet support Groovy 5.

### Module Dependencies

[](#module-dependencies)

Spring Boot 4.0 has [a new modular design](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/28/modularizing-spring-boot/) and now ships smaller focused modules rather than several large jars. As a result, this release has a more consistent set of “starter” POMs, and features that only relied on a third-party dependency to work can require an additional starter.

You will need to make dependency modifications if your current application doesn’t use Spring Boot “starter” POMs.

#### Main Code

[](#main-code)

The new modules and “starter” POMs follow a convention that lets you identify where the support for a given technology comes from:

- All Spring Boot modules are named `spring-boot-<technology>`.
- The root package of each module is `org.springframework.boot.<technology>`.
- All “starter” POMs are named `spring-boot-starter-<technology>`.

To illustrate the above, support for GraphQL is in `spring-boot-graphql` with a root package of `org.springframework.boot.graphql`. The “starter” POM is `spring-boot-starter-graphql`.

| Note | Review the list of “starter” POMs below based on the technologies that you are using and review your dependencies. You may face issue if you use a technology that previously had no “starter” POM.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />For instance, if you are using Flyway or Liquibase you used to only have the relevant third-party dependency. You now need to replace that with `spring-boot-starter-flyway` or `spring-boot-starter-liquibase`, respectively. |
|------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

#### Test Code

[](#test-code)

The modularity also applies to the test infrastructure. A similar convention is applied:

- All Spring Boot test modules are named `spring-boot-<technology>-test`.
- The root package of each such module is `org.springframework.boot.<technology>.test`.
- All test “starter” POMs are named `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test`.

To illustrate the above, test infrastructure for GraphQL is in `spring-boot-graphql-test` with a root package of `org.springframework.boot.graphql.test`. The “starter” POM is `spring-boot-starter-graphql-test`.

| Note | If you are using a technology that defines its own test infrastructure, you should swap it to the `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test` equivalent. In the example above, `spring-boot-graphql-starter-test` has a dependency on `org.springframework.graphql:spring-graphql-test`.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Not doing so could lead to issues that are hard to track. For example, `@WithMockUser` and `@WithUserDetails` from `spring-security-test` now requires `spring-boot-starter-security-test` to operate properly. |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

| Tip | Given that all test “starter” POMs bring `spring-boot-starter-test` transitively, you don’t need to define this starter anymore. Rather, you should list the starters of the technologies that are under test for the module. |
|-----|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

#### Starters

[](#starters)

This release harmonizes the use of starters in two ways:

- Most technologies covered by Spring Boot have a dedicated starter.
- Each starter has a test starter companion.

- ruleID: jackson-import-00010
  description: Jackson 3 uses tools.jackson package namespace; com.fasterxml.jackson is replaced
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4 uses Jackson 3 as its preferred JSON library. Jackson 3 uses new group IDs and package names with `com.fasterxml.jackson` becoming `tools.jackson`.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;
    import com.fasterxml.jackson.core.JsonProcessingException;
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import tools.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;
    import tools.jackson.core.JsonProcessingException;
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - **Exception:** The `jackson-annotations` module continues to use the `com.fasterxml.jackson.core` group ID and `com.fasterxml.jackson.annotation` package
    - For libraries that require Jackson 2, dependency management for Jackson 2 remains available
    - A Jackson 2 `ObjectMapper` can be used alongside Boot's Jackson 3 auto-configuration via the `spring-boot-jackson2` module
    - Jackson now auto-detects and registers ALL modules on the classpath (Spring Boot 3 only registered well-known modules). Disable with `spring.jackson.find-and-add-modules=false`
    - See the [Jackson 3 wiki](https://github.com/FasterXML/jackson/wiki/Jackson-Release-3.0#major-changesfeatures-in-30) for full details on changes
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#upgrading-jackson
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: com.fasterxml.jackson*
        location: PACKAGE

    ```java
        // ...
    ```

    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.jackson.ObjectValueSerializer;

        // ...
    }
    ```

    ```java
    @Bean
    ```

    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.jackson.JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer customizer() {

    ```

- ruleID: messaging-dependency-00010
  description: Reactive Pulsar support removed from Spring Boot 4; auto-configuration no longer available
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot no longer manages the reactive Pulsar client. Following the decision to remove reactor support in Spring Pulsar, auto-configuration for Spring Pulsar Reactive has been removed.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Remove the `spring-pulsar-reactive` dependency from your build file
    2. Migrate reactive Pulsar consumer/producer code to the imperative Spring Pulsar API using `spring-boot-starter-pulsar`
    3. If you require reactive streaming with Pulsar, manage the reactive client dependency and configuration manually

    ### Additional Info

    - The imperative Spring Pulsar API (`spring-boot-starter-pulsar`) is still fully supported
    - Auto-configuration for reactive Pulsar beans is no longer provided
    - Review [Spring for Apache Pulsar 2.0](https://docs.spring.io/spring-pulsar/reference/whats-new.html) release notes for additional changes
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#pulsar-reactive
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.pulsar.spring-pulsar-reactive
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: messaging-import-00010
  description: StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer removed; use Spring Kafka's StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer` has been removed in favor of Spring Kafka's `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.kafka.StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer customizer() {
        return factoryBean -> factoryBean.setCloseTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.kafka.config.StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer;

    @Bean
    public StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer configurer() {
        return factoryBean -> factoryBean.setCloseTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer` implements `Ordered` with a default value of `0`
    - Be aware of ordering if you have multiple configurers
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#kafka-streams-customization
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#kafka-streams-customization
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.kafka.StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: messaging-pattern-00010
  description: spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random removed; use spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Kafka has moved its retry capabilities from Spring Retry to Spring Framework. The property `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random` has been removed in favor of `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter`, which provides more flexibility.

    ### Migration Steps
    - Replace `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random` with `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter` in your configuration
    - The `jitter` property offers more flexibility than the boolean `random` property
    - See: https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/application-properties/index.html#application-properties.integration.spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-kafka-retry-features
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: spring\.kafka\.retry\.topic\.backoff\.random
        filePattern: application.*\.(properties|ya?ml)
- ruleID: messaging-import-00020
  description: RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer replaced by RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer and RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring AMQP has moved its retry capabilities from Spring Retry to Spring Framework. The `RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer` interface has been replaced by two dedicated customizers.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer retryCustomizer() {
        return (target, retryTemplate) -> {
            // customize based on target
        };
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    // For RabbitTemplate retry customization:
    @Bean
    public RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer templateRetryCustomizer() {
        return settings -> { /* customize */ };
    }

    // For RabbitListener retry customization:
    @Bean
    public RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer listenerRetryCustomizer() {
        return settings -> { /* customize */ };
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Choose `RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer` for template retry settings
    - Choose `RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer` for listener retry settings
    - If you customized by target, split your logic into the appropriate customizer
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-amqp-retry-features
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-amqp-retry-features
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer
        location: IMPORT

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-111421/rules/server.yaml
- ruleID: server-dependency-00010
  description: Undertow support dropped in Spring Boot 4; not compatible with Servlet 6.1
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Undertow support has been dropped from Spring Boot 4.0 because Undertow is not yet compatible with the Servlet 6.1 baseline that Spring Boot 4 requires.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Remove the `spring-boot-starter-undertow` dependency from your build file
    2. Switch to Tomcat (default) by using `spring-boot-starter-web` / `spring-boot-starter-webmvc`, or use Jetty with `spring-boot-starter-jetty`
    3. Review any Undertow-specific configuration properties (prefixed with `server.undertow.`) and remove or replace them
    4. Test your application with the new embedded server

    ### Additional Info

    - Spring Boot 4 requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline (Jakarta EE 11)
    - Tomcat is the default embedded server and is fully compatible
    - Jetty is available as an alternative via `spring-boot-starter-jetty`
    - Do not deploy Spring Boot 4 applications to non-Servlet 6.1 compliant containers
    - Any Undertow-specific programmatic configuration (e.g., `UndertowServletWebServerFactory` customization) must be replaced with the equivalent for your chosen server
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#undertow
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-starter-undertow
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-111421/rules/session.yaml
- ruleID: session-dependency-00010
  description: Spring Session Hazelcast support removed from Spring Boot; now under Hazelcast team leadership
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Direct support for Spring Session Hazelcast has been removed from Spring Boot 4. The project is now under the [leadership of the Hazelcast team](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/14/spring-session-hazelcast-new-leadership).

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Spring Boot no longer provides auto-configuration for Spring Session Hazelcast
    2. If you need Hazelcast-backed sessions, depend on the Hazelcast-maintained version of `spring-session-hazelcast` with an explicit version
    3. You may need to provide manual session configuration since Spring Boot auto-configuration is removed

    ### Additional Info

    - The Hazelcast team now maintains and publishes `spring-session-hazelcast`
    - Explicit version management is required since Spring Boot no longer manages the version
    - Consider alternative session stores if Hazelcast-backed sessions are not essential (e.g., Redis via `spring-boot-starter-session-data-redis`, JDBC via `spring-boot-starter-session-jdbc`)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-session-hazelcast
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.session.spring-session-hazelcast
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: session-dependency-00020
  description: Spring Session MongoDB support removed from Spring Boot; now under MongoDB team leadership
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3

  message: |-

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Spring Boot no longer provides auto-configuration for Spring Session MongoDB
    2. If you need MongoDB-backed sessions, depend on the MongoDB-maintained version of `spring-session-data-mongodb` with an explicit version
    3. You may need to provide manual session configuration since Spring Boot auto-configuration is removed

    ### Additional Info

    - The MongoDB team now maintains and publishes `spring-session-data-mongodb`
    - Explicit version management is required since Spring Boot no longer manages the version
    - Consider alternative session stores if MongoDB-backed sessions are not essential (e.g., Redis via `spring-boot-starter-session-data-redis`, JDBC via `spring-boot-starter-session-jdbc`)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-session-mongodb
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.session.spring-session-data-mongodb
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

  description: Spring Boot Spock integration removed; Spock does not yet support Groovy 5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's Spock integration has been removed because Spock does not yet support Groovy 5, which is required by Spring Boot 4.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. If your tests use Spock with Spring Boot's test integration, you will need to migrate to JUnit 5 or wait for Spock to support Groovy 5
    2. Remove `spock-spring` and any related Spock test dependencies
    3. Rewrite Spock specifications as JUnit 5 test classes
    4. Replace Spock's `@SpringBootTest` integration with JUnit 5's equivalent annotations

    ### Additional Info

    - Spock's `@SpringBootTest` and related test infrastructure is no longer supported
    - JUnit 5 is the recommended testing framework for Spring Boot 4
    - Monitor the [Spock project](https://github.com/spockframework/spock) for Groovy 5 support updates
    - Spring Boot's test starter (`spring-boot-starter-test`) includes JUnit 5 by default
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spock-integration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.spockframework.spock-spring
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: testing-import-00010
  description: MockitoTestExecutionListener removed; use MockitoExtension from Mockito
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `MockitoTestExecutionListener` deprecated in Spring Boot 3.4 has been removed. If your `@Mock` or `@Captor` annotated fields aren't working as expected, use `MockitoExtension` from Mockito.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.test.mock.mockito.MockitoTestExecutionListener;

    @TestExecutionListeners(MockitoTestExecutionListener.class)
    public class MyTest {
        @Mock
        private MyService myService;
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.mockito.junit.jupiter.MockitoExtension;

    @ExtendWith(MockitoExtension.class)
    public class MyTest {
        @Mock
        private MyService myService;
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The listener was only indirectly used, so deprecation warnings were easy to miss
    - `@Mock` and `@Captor` fields will stop working without `MockitoExtension`
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#mockito-captor-and-mock-annotations
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#mockito-captor-and-mock-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.test.mock.mockito.MockitoTestExecutionListener
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: testing-import-00020
  description: '@SpringBootTest no longer auto-configures MockMvc; add @AutoConfigureMockMvc'
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Using `@SpringBootTest` will no longer provide any MockMVC support. If you want to use MockMVC in your tests, you must add `@AutoConfigureMockMvc` annotation to the test class.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc;

    @SpringBootTest
    public class MyControllerTest {
        @Autowired
        private MockMvc mockMvc; // Auto-configured by @SpringBootTest
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc;
    import org.springframework.boot.test.autoconfigure.web.servlet.AutoConfigureMockMvc;

    @SpringBootTest
    @AutoConfigureMockMvc
    public class MyControllerTest {
        @Autowired
        private MockMvc mockMvc; // Now requires @AutoConfigureMockMvc
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - HtmlUnit settings have moved under an `htmlUnit` attribute in `@AutoConfigureMockMvc`
    - Old: `@AutoConfigureMockMvc(webClientEnabled=false, webDriverEnabled=false)`
    - New: `@AutoConfigureMockMvc(htmlUnit = @HtmlUnit(webClient = false, webDriver = false))`
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#using-mockmvc-and-springboottest
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#using-mockmvc-and-springboottest
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc
        location: IMPORT


    ### After

    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#using-mockmvc-and-springboottest

  description: TestRestTemplate moved to new package; add spring-boot-resttestclient dependency
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot

  message: |-
    The `TestRestTemplate` class has been relocated to `org.springframework.boot.resttestclient.TestRestTemplate`. Additionally, `@SpringBootTest` no longer auto-configures `TestRestTemplate` beans.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.test.web.client.TestRestTemplate;

    @SpringBootTest(webEnvironment = SpringBootTest.WebEnvironment.RANDOM_PORT)
    public class MyIntegrationTest {
        @Autowired
        private TestRestTemplate restTemplate;
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.resttestclient.TestRestTemplate;
    import org.springframework.boot.test.web.client.AutoConfigureTestRestTemplate;

    @SpringBootTest(webEnvironment = SpringBootTest.WebEnvironment.RANDOM_PORT)
    @AutoConfigureTestRestTemplate
    public class MyIntegrationTest {
        @Autowired
        private TestRestTemplate restTemplate;
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Add test-scoped dependency on `org.springframework.boot:spring-boot-resttestclient`

- ruleID: web-import-00010
  description: PathRequest.toStaticResources now includes /fonts/**; review security settings
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    If you use `PathRequest.toStaticResources()`, be aware that Spring Boot 4.0 adds a `/fonts/**` location. This path will have the same security settings as your other static resource locations.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest;

    // /fonts/** was NOT included as a static resource location
    pathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest;
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.web.servlet.StaticResourceLocation;

    // /fonts/** IS now included; exclude if not wanted
    pathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations().excluding(StaticResourceLocation.FONTS);
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The new `/fonts/**` location has the same security settings as previously configured static locations
    - Only exclude if you specifically do not want fonts served as static resources
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#fonts-added-to-common-static-locations
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#fonts-added-to-common-static-locations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: web-import-00020
  description: HttpMessageConverters is deprecated; use ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer or ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer
  category: optional
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's `HttpMessageConverters` class is deprecated because Spring Framework improved the converter configuration. Contributing `HttpMessageConverter` beans to the context is no longer supported.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.http.HttpMessageConverters;

    @Bean
    public HttpMessageConverters customConverters() {
        return new HttpMessageConverters(new MyCustomConverter());
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    @Bean
    public ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer clientCustomizer() {
        return converters -> converters.addCustom(new MyCustomConverter());
    }

    @Bean
    public ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer serverCustomizer() {
        return converters -> converters.addCustom(new MyCustomConverter());
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Custom `HttpMessageConverters` beans are still supported but the type is deprecated
    - Contributing individual `HttpMessageConverter` beans to the context is no longer supported
    - Use `ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer` for client-side converters
    - Use `ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer` for server-side converters
    - See: https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/web/servlet.html#web.servlet.spring-mvc.message-converters
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#httpmessageconverters-deprecation
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.http.HttpMessageConverters
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: web-pattern-00010
  description: server.forward-headers-strategy no longer has effect in WAR deployments
  category: potential
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `server.forward-headers-strategy` property no longer has an effect when deploying a WAR file to an external container. If you were relying on `server.forward-headers-strategy=framework` in a WAR deployment, you must now define the `ForwardedHeaderFilter` bean yourself.

    ### Before
    ```properties
    server.forward-headers-strategy=framework
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    @Bean
    FilterRegistrationBean<ForwardedHeaderFilter> forwardedHeaderFilter() {
        ForwardedHeaderFilter filter = new ForwardedHeaderFilter();
        FilterRegistrationBean<ForwardedHeaderFilter> registration = new FilterRegistrationBean<>(filter);
        registration.setDispatcherTypes(DispatcherType.REQUEST, DispatcherType.ASYNC, DispatcherType.ERROR);
        registration.setOrder(Ordered.HIGHEST_PRECEDENCE);
        return registration;
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - This only affects WAR deployments to external containers; embedded server deployments are unaffected
    - The property still works for non-WAR deployments
    - See: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#forwarded-headers-strategy
  links:

- ruleID: api-import-00010
  description: Log4j 1 org.apache.log4j package renamed to org.apache.logging.log4j in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |
    Log4j 2 uses the `org.apache.logging.log4j` package namespace instead of `org.apache.log4j`. All imports from the old namespace must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.Logger;
    import org.apache.log4j.LogManager;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger;
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 2 is a complete rewrite with a new package namespace
    - Most class names are the same; some classes were renamed (MDC, NDC, Priority, Category)
    - The configuration file format is also incompatible and must be converted separately
    - Log4j 1 reached End of Life in 2015 and no longer receives security fixes
    - See the [migration guide](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html) for full details

    ### Specific replacements

    | Old class | Replacement |
    |---|---|
    | `org.apache.log4j.varia.DenyAllFilter` | Log4j 2 DenyAllFilter |
    | `org.apache.log4j.varia.LevelMatchFilter` | Log4j 2 LevelMatchFilter |
    | `org.apache.log4j.varia.LevelRangeFilter` | Log4j 2 LevelRangeFilter |
    | `org.apache.log4j.varia.StringMatchFilter` | Log4j 2 StringMatchFilter or RegexFilter |
    | `org.apache.log4j.varia.NullAppender` | Log4j 2 NullAppender |
    | `org.apache.log4j.rolling.SizeBasedTriggeringPolicy` | Log4j 2 SizeBasedTriggeringPolicy |
    | `org.apache.log4j.PatternLayout` | Log4j 2 PatternLayout |
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j
        location: PACKAGE
- ruleID: api-import-00020
  description: org.apache.log4j.MDC replaced by org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.MDC` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` in Log4j 2. The class name changed, not just the package.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.MDC;

    MDC.put("user", username);
    String user = (String) MDC.get("user");
    MDC.remove("user");
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext;

    ThreadContext.put("user", username);
    String user = ThreadContext.get("user");
    ThreadContext.remove("user");
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `ThreadContext` combines the functionality of both `MDC` and `NDC` from Log4j 1
    - The `ThreadContext.put()` method replaces `MDC.put()`
    - The `ThreadContext.push()`/`pop()` methods replace `NDC.push()`/`pop()`
    - `ThreadContext.get()` returns `String` directly, unlike `MDC.get()` which returned `Object`
    - See [ThreadContext documentation](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/thread-context.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.MDC
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: api-import-00030
  description: org.apache.log4j.NDC replaced by org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.NDC` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` in Log4j 2. Use `ThreadContext.push()` and `ThreadContext.pop()` instead of `NDC.push()` and `NDC.pop()`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.NDC;

    NDC.push("context");
    // ... logging ...
    NDC.pop();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext;

    ThreadContext.push("context");
    // ... logging ...
    ThreadContext.pop();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `ThreadContext` combines the functionality of both `MDC` and `NDC` from Log4j 1
    - The stack-based context (NDC) and map-based context (MDC) are unified in `ThreadContext`
    - `ThreadContext.push()`/`pop()` replaces `NDC.push()`/`pop()`
    - `ThreadContext.peek()` replaces `NDC.peek()`
    - See [ThreadContext documentation](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/thread-context.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.NDC
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: api-import-00040
  description: org.apache.log4j.Priority replaced by org.apache.logging.log4j.Level
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2

    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.Priority` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.Level` in Log4j 2. The `Priority` class was already deprecated in Log4j 1 in favor of `Level`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.Priority;

    if (logger.isEnabledFor(Priority.WARN)) {
        logger.warn("Warning message");
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Level;

    if (logger.isEnabled(Level.WARN)) {
        logger.warn("Warning message");
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `Priority` was deprecated in Log4j 1; `Level` is the direct replacement
    - Log4j 2 `Level` provides the same standard levels: TRACE, DEBUG, INFO, WARN, ERROR, FATAL
    - Custom levels are supported via `Level.forName()`
    - See [Level documentation](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/customloglevels.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.Priority
        location: IMPORT

- ruleID: appenders-import-00030
  description: Log4j 1 DailyRollingFileAppender replaced by Log4j 2 RollingFile with TimeBasedTriggeringPolicy

  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.DailyRollingFileAppender` from Log4j 1 has been replaced by the Log4j 2 `RollingFile` appender with a `TimeBasedTriggeringPolicy`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.DailyRollingFileAppender;
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <RollingFile name="RollingFile" fileName="app.log" filePattern="app.%d{yyyy-MM-dd}">
        <PatternLayout pattern="%d %p %c{1.} [%t] %m%n"/>
        <TimeBasedTriggeringPolicy/>
        <DefaultRolloverStrategy fileIndex="min"/>
    </RollingFile>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Use `filePattern="app.%d{yyyy-MM-dd}"` to match the daily rolling behavior.
    - Set `DefaultRolloverStrategy fileIndex="min"` to replicate Log4j 1's indexing behavior.
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#configuration-appenders

output/log4j1-to-log4j2-20260624-130324/rules/bridge.yaml
- ruleID: bridge-dependency-00010
  description: log4j-over-slf4j must be removed before installing the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge (`log4j-1.2-api`) replaces Log4j 1 classes and is incompatible with `org.slf4j:log4j-over-slf4j`. Both artifacts provide alternative implementations of the `org.apache.log4j.*` classes, so having both on the classpath causes conflicts.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Remove the `org.slf4j:log4j-over-slf4j` dependency from your `pom.xml` or `build.gradle`
    2. Add the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge dependency:
       ```xml
       <dependency>
         <groupId>org.apache.logging.log4j</groupId>
         <artifactId>log4j-1.2-api</artifactId>
         <scope>runtime</scope>
       </dependency>
       ```
    3. If you still need SLF4J support, use `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-slf4j2-impl` instead to route SLF4J calls through Log4j 2

    ### Additional Info

    - `log4j-over-slf4j` routes Log4j 1 calls to SLF4J; `log4j-1.2-api` routes them to Log4j 2 API instead
    - If your application uses SLF4J as its primary logging facade, consider using Log4j 2 as the SLF4J backend via `log4j-slf4j2-impl`
    - After fully migrating to Log4j 2 API and configuration, the bridge can be removed
    - See [Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge installation](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#log4j-1-2-api-installation)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#log4j-1-2-api-installation
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.slf4j.log4j-over-slf4j
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

output/log4j1-to-log4j2-20260624-130324/rules/config.yaml
- ruleID: config-pattern-00010
  description: Log4j 1 configuration files must be converted to Log4j 2 format
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Log4j 2 uses a new configuration file format that is incompatible with Log4j 1. The `log4j.properties` or `log4j.xml` configuration files must be converted to the Log4j 2 format.

    ### Migration Steps
    - Convert `log4j.properties` to `log4j2.properties`, `log4j2.xml`, `log4j2.json`, or `log4j2.yaml`
    - Log4j 2 configuration files have a different structure and element names
    - The Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge can convert some configurations at runtime, but manual conversion is recommended

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 2 supports XML, JSON, YAML, and properties configuration formats
    - The default configuration file name is `log4j2.xml` (or `log4j2.properties`, etc.)
    - Appender and layout configurations have different element names and attributes
    - See [Configuration documentation](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/configuration.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#configuration-file-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: log4j\.properties|log4j\.xml
        filePattern: .*
- ruleID: config-import-00010
  description: Log4j1ConfigurationConverter converts log4j.properties to log4j2.xml format
  category: optional
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `Log4j1ConfigurationConverter` utility converts Log4j 1 configuration files (`log4j.properties`) to Log4j 2 format (`log4j2.xml`). This is a one-time migration tool provided by the `log4j-1.2-api` bridge.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Ensure `log4j-api`, `log4j-core`, and `log4j-1.2-api` are on the classpath.
    2. Run: `java org.apache.log4j.config.Log4j1ConfigurationConverter --in log4j.properties --out log4j2.xml`
    3. Review the generated `log4j2.xml` and adjust as needed.
    4. Remove the old `log4j.properties` file once the conversion is verified.

    ### Additional Info
    - This utility is part of the `log4j-1.2-api` bridge artifact.
    - The conversion may not handle all Log4j 1 configuration features; review the output carefully.
    - After conversion, consider removing the `log4j-1.2-api` dependency if no other Log4j 1 APIs are used.
    - See the [Log4j 2 Configuration Guide](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/configuration.html) for the full Log4j 2 configuration syntax.
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.config.Log4j1ConfigurationConverter
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: config-pattern-00020
  description: Log4j 1 log4j.properties config file must be converted to Log4j 2 format
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `log4j.properties` configuration file uses Log4j 1 format and must be converted to Log4j 2 format (e.g., `log4j2.xml`, `log4j2.properties`, or `log4j2.yaml`).

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Use `Log4j1ConfigurationConverter` to auto-convert: `java org.apache.log4j.config.Log4j1ConfigurationConverter --in log4j.properties --out log4j2.xml`
    2. Alternatively, rewrite the configuration manually using Log4j 2 syntax.
    3. Replace `${foo}` interpolation syntax with `${sys:foo}` for system properties.
    4. Update appender and layout class references to Log4j 2 equivalents.

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 2 supports multiple configuration formats: XML, JSON, YAML, and properties.
    - The `log4j-1.2-api` bridge can parse Log4j 1 config files at runtime if `log4j1.compatibility=true` is set.
    - See [Log4j 2 Configuration](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/configuration.html) for the new format.
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: log4j\.properties
        filePattern: .*
- ruleID: config-pattern-00030
  description: Log4j 1 ${foo} interpolation must be changed to ${sys:foo} in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Log4j 1 uses `${foo}` syntax for system property interpolation. Log4j 2 extends this mechanism with pluggable Lookups and requires the `sys:` prefix for system properties.

    ### Before
    ```properties
    log4j.appender.file.File=${logDir}/app.log
    ```

    ### After
    ```properties
    log4j.appender.file.File=${sys:logDir}/app.log
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 2 supports many lookup types: `sys:` (system properties), `env:` (environment variables), `jndi:`, `ctx:` (ThreadContext), etc.
    - All occurrences of `${foo}` in Log4j 1 config files should be replaced with `${sys:foo}`.
    - See [Log4j 2 Lookups](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/lookups.html) for available lookup types.
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#configuration-interpolation
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: \$\{[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9_.]*\}
        filePattern: log4j.*\.(properties|xml)
- ruleID: config-import-00020
  description: Log4j 1 PropertyConfigurator replaced by Log4j 2 Configurator or bridge compatibility mode
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.PropertyConfigurator` from Log4j 1 is used for programmatic configuration. In Log4j 2, use the `Configurator` class or enable bridge compatibility mode.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.PropertyConfigurator;
    PropertyConfigurator.configure("log4j.properties");
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.core.config.Configurator;
    Configurator.initialize(null, "log4j2.xml");
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The bridge's `PropertyConfigurator` support requires `log4j1.compatibility=true` (since 2.24.0).
    - For new projects, prefer migrating to Log4j 2 native configuration.
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#log4j1.compatibility
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.PropertyConfigurator
        location: IMPORT

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: Replace log4j:log4j with org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `log4j:log4j` artifact (Log4j 1.x) has reached End of Life and must be replaced with `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core` (Log4j 2.x).

    ### Migration Steps
    - Remove the `log4j:log4j` dependency from your POM or build file
    - Add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core` as a replacement
    - If using Log4j 1 API in your code, also add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-api`
    - Convert your Log4j 1 configuration files to the Log4j 2 format

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 1 has been EOL since August 2015 and no longer receives security fixes
    - Log4j 2 uses a completely different configuration format
    - If you cannot migrate immediately, consider using the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge
    - See [Installation guide](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/installation.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#backend-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: log4j.log4j
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    ### Migration Steps
    - Remove the `ch.qos.reload4j:reload4j` dependency from your POM or build file
    - Add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core` as a replacement
    - If using Log4j 1 API in your code, also add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-api`
    - Convert your Log4j 1 configuration files to the Log4j 2 format

    ### Additional Info
    - reload4j is a drop-in replacement for Log4j 1.x but is still based on the old architecture
    - Log4j 2 provides better performance, more flexible configuration, and active security support
    - If you cannot migrate immediately, consider using the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge
    - See [Installation guide](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/installation.html)

    - Use `log4j-slf4j2-impl` for SLF4J 2.x; use `log4j-slf4j-impl` for SLF4J 1.x
    - The SLF4J API (`org.slf4j:slf4j-api`) remains unchanged

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00050
  description: Upgrade commons-logging to 1.3.0+ or replace with log4j-jcl for Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2

  message: |-
    When migrating from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2, the `commons-logging:commons-logging` dependency needs to be updated to route logging through Log4j 2.

    ### Migration Steps
    - **Option 1:** Upgrade `commons-logging:commons-logging` to version 1.3.0 or later (which natively supports Log4j 2)
    - **Option 2:** Replace `commons-logging:commons-logging` with `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-jcl` (the Log4j 2 JCL bridge)

    ### Additional Info
    - Commons Logging 1.3.0+ includes native support for routing to Log4j 2
    - The `log4j-jcl` bridge provides the same functionality for older Commons Logging versions
    - Only one of these options is needed, not both
    - See [Installation guide](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/installation.html)
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#backend-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: commons-logging.commons-logging
        upperbound: 1.3.0
