case-004-tomcat9-to-tomcat10 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $7.18 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The output captures the vast majority of migration artifacts from the guide. All 5 package rename changes (javax.servlet→jakarta.servlet, javax.servlet.jsp→jakarta.servlet.jsp, javax.el→jakarta.el, javax.websocket→jakarta.websocket, javax.security.auth.message→jakarta.security.auth.message) are captured. The GenericPrincipal.getPassword() removal, web.xml default encoding change, session persistence default change, HTTP/2 connector deduplication, access log %D pattern change, AsyncLoggerPollInterval removal, HostConfig.check() semantics change, CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee caching change, and multi-part upload direct memory requirement are all covered. Minor omissions include: (1) The 'System properties' section mentions broadly that many Tomcat-specific system properties were replaced with component attributes, but no specific pattern captures this general change beyond AsyncLoggerPollInterval. (2) The 'Logging' section notes that the logging implementation now only creates log files once there is something to write - this behavioral change has no pattern. (3) The 'Internal APIs' section notes broad incompatibility beyond just GenericPrincipal.getPassword(), but this is inherently vague. (4) The legacyAppBase/webapps-javaee deployment-time conversion mechanism is mentioned in the guide but not captured as a distinct pattern (though it's referenced in the servlet-import-00010 message). These are relatively minor gaps - the system properties and logging file creation changes are the most notable concrete omissions.

patterns_qualityPASS

14 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 14 rules, 100% pass rate

rule_correctness5

I reviewed all 10 rule YAML files (config.yaml with 2 rules, deployment.yaml, el.yaml, jsp.yaml, logging.yaml with 2 rules, security.yaml with 3 rules, servlet.yaml with 2 rules, session.yaml, websocket.yaml). Here is the assessment:

When condition accuracy: All rules correctly match source-side (Tomcat 9 / javax) artifacts. The java.referenced rules use correct patterns like javax.servlet (PACKAGE), javax.el (PACKAGE), javax.websocket* (PACKAGE), org.apache.catalina.realm.GenericPrincipal.getPassword (METHOD_CALL), javax.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig (ANNOTATION). The builtin rules appropriately use builtin.xml with XPath for web.xml elements and builtin.filecontent with regex patterns for server.xml and properties files. No rule matches target-side code.

Message quality: Every rule provides clear explanation of WHAT changed, WHY (migration from Java EE to Jakarta EE, or Tomcat behavioral changes), and HOW to migrate with specific steps. The core namespace migration rules (servlet, jsp, el, websocket, security-import) all include well-formatted before/after Java code examples. Even non-code rules like config-xml-00010, logging-pattern-00010, and config-pattern-00010 include before/after XML examples or clear migration steps. The GenericPrincipal.getPassword rule explains the removal and suggests alternative approaches.

Documentation URLs: All URLs point to specific sections of the migration guide (e.g., migration-10.html#Servlet_5.0_API, migration-10.html#Pages_3.0, migration-10.html#Expression_Language_4.0, migration-10.html#Internal_APIs, migration-10.html#Access_Log_Patterns). The CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee rule links to the specific Bugzilla issue. None are generic homepage links.

Category and effort: Mandatory category is correctly applied to the namespace changes (javax→jakarta) and the removed API (GenericPrincipal.getPassword). Potential category is correctly used for behavioral changes (encoding defaults, session persistence, HTTP/2 config, access log patterns, caching behavior). Effort values are reasonable: 5 for code changes requiring recompilation, 3 for configuration review, 1 for trivial pattern/property changes.

No hallucinations: All source artifacts are verified real - javax.servlet-api:4.0.1, javax.servlet.jsp-api:2.3.3, javax.el-api:3.0.0, javax.websocket-api:1.1, javax.security.auth.message-api:1.1 all exist. GenericPrincipal.getPassword() exists in Tomcat 9's catalina. HostConfig.check() exists. StandardManager exists. The verify-results.json confirms 9 verified, 0 not_found. All 14 tests pass at 100%.

The only very minor observation is that the servlet-import-00010 rule with javax.servlet pattern could theoretically also match javax.servlet.jsp packages, but the JSP rule with javax.servlet.jsp* provides more specific guidance, so both firing is actually beneficial. This is a negligible concern that doesn't affect correctness.

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/config.yaml
- ruleID: config-xml-00010
  description: Default request/response character encoding changed to UTF-8 in Tomcat 10
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10, `conf/web.xml` sets the default request and response character encoding to UTF-8. Previously, the default was ISO-8859-1.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review your application's character encoding requirements.
    2. If your application relied on the old ISO-8859-1 default encoding, you may need to explicitly set the encoding in your application's `web.xml`.
    3. If your application already uses UTF-8 (or sets encoding explicitly), no changes are needed.

    ### Additional Info

    - Applications that explicitly set `<request-character-encoding>` or `<response-character-encoding>` in their `web.xml` should verify their settings are still correct.
    - Applications that relied on the default ISO-8859-1 encoding without explicitly setting it may experience encoding issues.
    - This change aligns Tomcat with the Servlet 5.0 specification default.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#web.xml_defaults
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#web.xml_defaults
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='request-character-encoding' or local-name()='response-character-encoding']
        filepaths:
            - web.xml
            - WEB-INF/web.xml
- ruleID: config-pattern-00010
  description: HTTP/2 duplicated configuration settings removed; now inherited from HTTP/1.1 connector
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10, configuration settings that were duplicated between the HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 connectors have been removed from the HTTP/2 connector. The HTTP/2 connector (`Http2Protocol`) now inherits these settings from the associated HTTP/1.1 connector.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review your `server.xml` for `<UpgradeProtocol className="org.apache.coyote.http2.Http2Protocol">` elements.
    2. Remove any attributes from the HTTP/2 UpgradeProtocol element that duplicate settings on the parent HTTP/1.1 Connector element.
    3. Ensure the desired values are set on the HTTP/1.1 Connector element instead.

    ### Additional Info

    - Settings like `maxHeaderSize`, `maxConcurrentStreams`, and other duplicated attributes should now be on the Connector element.
    - The HTTP/2 protocol will automatically inherit these from the associated HTTP/1.1 connector.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#HTTP/2
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#HTTP/2
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: org\.apache\.coyote\.http2\.Http2Protocol
        filePattern: .*server\.xml

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/deployment.yaml
- ruleID: deployment-method-00010
  description: HostConfig.check(String) semantics changed in Tomcat 10.0.3
  category: potential
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10.0.3 onwards, the semantics of `HostConfig.check(String)` have changed. The method now marks the application as serviced before checking resources and un-marks it after the checks are complete. If the application is already marked as serviced when the method is called, the method will be a NO-OP.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review any custom code that calls `HostConfig.check(String)` directly.
    2. Update your code to account for the new semantics — the method now handles serviced-state management internally.
    3. Remove any manual `setServiced(true)` / `setServiced(false)` calls around `HostConfig.check()` invocations.

    ### Additional Info

    - Previously, callers were expected to mark the application as serviced before calling `check(String)`.
    - The new behavior is self-contained: `check(String)` manages its own serviced state.
    - If the application is already marked as serviced, the method will be a NO-OP, preventing concurrent checks.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.catalina.startup.HostConfig.check
        location: METHOD_CALL

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/el.yaml
- ruleID: el-import-00010
  description: javax.el package renamed to jakarta.el in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Expression Language API package has changed from `javax.el` to `jakarta.el` in Tomcat 10 (Expression Language 4.0). All imports and type references using `javax.el` must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import javax.el.ELContext;
    import javax.el.ExpressionFactory;
    import javax.el.ValueExpression;

    public class ElHelper {
        public Object evaluate(String expression) {
            ExpressionFactory factory = ExpressionFactory.newInstance();
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import jakarta.el.ELContext;
    import jakarta.el.ExpressionFactory;
    import jakarta.el.ValueExpression;

    public class ElHelper {
        public Object evaluate(String expression) {
            ExpressionFactory factory = ExpressionFactory.newInstance();
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All classes under `javax.el` must be migrated to `jakarta.el`
    - This affects custom EL resolvers, EL functions, and any code that programmatically interacts with the Expression Language API
    - Web applications must be recompiled against the new Jakarta Expression Language 4.0 API
    - The Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE can automate this conversion
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Expression_Language_4.0
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.el*
        location: PACKAGE

The user can override `checkpoint_behavior` explicitly.\n34\t\n35\t## Returns\n36\t\n37\t- `rules_dir` \u2014 Path to generated rule YAML files\n38\t- `tests_dir` \u2014 Path to test data\n39\t- `report` \u2014 Path to report.yaml\n40\t- `summary` \u2014 Markdown summary table with:\n41\t  - rules_count, passed, failed, pass_rate\n42\t  - coverage_report (sections processed/skipped)\n43\t  - fix_iterations used\n44\t\n45\t## Execution Modes\n46\t\n47\t- `interactive` mode: ask at checkpoint only when `checkpoint_behavior=ask`\n48\t- `non_interactive` mode: never prompt the user; obey `checkpoint_behavior`\n49\t  - `continue`: run full pipeline\n50\t  - `stop_after_extract`: end after extraction/coverage with untested outputs\n51\t  - `ask`: treated as `continue` (no prompt allowed in non-interactive mode)\n52\t\n53\t## References\n54\t\n55\t- `references/orchestrator-details.md` \u2014 status-line conventions, parallelism defaults, resume preconditions, rebuild behavior\n56\t\n57\t## Permissions\n58\t\n59\t| Operation | Pattern | Purpose |\n60\t|-----------|---------|---------|\n61\t| shell | `mkdir -p output` | Create output directory |\n62\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/ingest *` | Fetch migration guide as markdown |\n63\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sections *` | Index guide sections with classification |\n64\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/merge-patterns *` | Merge partial patterns files |\n65\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/contract-validate *` | Validate sub-agent payload contracts |\n66\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/verify *` | Verify patterns against source artifacts |\n67\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/construct *` | Build rule YAML from patterns.json |\n68\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/validate *` | Validate rule YAML structure |\n69\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/scaffold *` | Create test directories and manifests |\n70\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sanitize *` | Fix XML comments in test data |\n71\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/test *` | Run kantra tests |\n72\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/report *` | Generate summary report with per-rule status |\n73\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/coverage *` | Check guide coverage |\n74\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/log *` | Append orchestrator events to pipeline log |\n75\t| shell | `ls *` | List files and directories |\n76\t| read | `output/**` | Read manifest, test results |\n77\t| write | `output/**` | Write migration artifacts |\n78\t\n79\t**Do NOT use `python`, `python3`, `node`, or any scripting language runtime.**\n80\t**Do NOT use `grep`, `sed`, `awk`, `wc`, `find`, or other shell text-processing tools to parse data that CLI commands already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation \u2014 do NOT retry the same operation with different syntax (heredocs, base64 encoding, helper scripts, etc.). A permission denial means the action is blocked, not that the syntax was wrong. Move to the next pipeline step or end the pipeline.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` first (use the pipeline timestamp to avoid collisions when multiple invocations run in parallel), read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

Protocol\n15\t\n16\t## Status Line Format\n17\t\n18\tUse concise status lines:\n19\t\n20\t```text\n21\t[step-name] message\n22\t```\n23\t\n24\tExample:\n25\t\n26\t```text\n27\t[ingest] Fetching guide `rule-writer` invocations\n42\t- Test generation: 1-5 parallel `test-generator` invocations\n43\t- Balance by rule/section count per worker\n44\t\n45\t## Resume Stage Preconditions\n46\t\n47\tThese are the canonical artifact checks for `resume_from`:\n48\t\n49\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n50\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n51\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n52\t- `test` requires and do not infer\n56\tor regenerate stages implicitly unless explicitly instructed.\n57\t\n58\t## Rebuild Behavior\n59\t\n60\t- `force_rebuild=true` means regenerate current stage outputs even if present.\n61\t- `force_rebuild=false` means reuse existing artifacts when preconditions hold.\n62\t\n63\t## Pipeline Transcript\n64\t\n65\tThe pipeline log (`<migration_dir>/pipeline.log`) captures the full session. **All logging goes through CLI commands** \u2014 no manual `echo >>` or shell variable assignments.\n66\t\n67\t### CLI command logging (automatic)\n68\t\n69\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` invocation auto-logs its JSON output when you pass `--log`. Pass `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>` to every CLI invocation. Substitute actual paths and values directly \u2014 do not use shell variables. Sub-agents pass their own `--agent` and `--model` values.\n70\t\n71\t### Orchestrator event logging (via cmd/log)\n72\t\n73\tLog agent-level events using `cmd/log` instead of shell echo commands:\n74\t\n75\t```bash\n76\tgo run ./cmd/log --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --message \"<message>\"\n77\t```\n78\t\n79\tEvents to log:\n80\t- Pipeline start: guide source, detected source/target/language\n81\t- Every `[step]` status line (start and done)\n82\t- Sub-agent dispatches: skill name, chunk number, agent name, model\n83\t- Sub-agent returns: patterns_count, files_written, errors, suspected_kantra_limitations\n84\t- Errors, retries, and partial failures\n85\t- Final summary table\n86\t\n87\t### Sub-agent CLI invocations\n88\t\n89\tWhen a sub-agent invokes a CLI command (e.g., rule-validator running `cmd/test`), the sub-agent passes its own identity:\n90\t\n91\t```bash\n92\tgo run ./cmd/test --rules ... --tests ... --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent rule-validator --model <agent_model>\n93\t```\n94\t\n95\tThis ensures every log entry is traceable to which agent ran it and which LLM powered the decision.\n96\t\n97\t## Timing\n98\t\n99\tTrack wall-clock elapsed time for the pipeline and each major stage. Record the current time (HH:MM:SS) at the start of the pipeline and at the start/end of each stage.\n100\t\n101\t**Pipeline timer:** Record start time before step 1. Print total elapsed in the final summary.\n102\t\n103\t**Stage timers:** For each stage, include elapsed time in the \"Done\" status line using the format `(<elapsed>)` where elapsed is `Xm Ys` (e.g. `2m 15s`). Omit hours unless the stage takes \u2265 60 minutes.\n104\t\n105\tFormat:\n106\t```\n107\t[step] Done \u2014 <metrics> (<elapsed>)\n108\t```\n109\t\n110\tStages to time:\n111\t- **ingest** \u2014 from guide fetch start to guide written\n112\t- **extract** \u2014 from section indexing start to rules constructed + validated (includes parallel rule-writer agents, merge, construct, validate)\n113\t- **coverage** \u2014 from coverage check start to re-extraction complete (or \"No gaps found\")\n114\t- **test-gen** \u2014 from scaffold start to all test-generator agents complete + sanitize\n115\t- **validate** \u2014 from first `cmd/test` run to fix loop complete (includes all fix iterations)\n116\t- **report** \u2014 from report generation start to report written\n117\t\n118\t## Sub-agent Protocol\n119\t\n120\tThis orchestrator delegates heavy LLM work to sub-agents using **invoke blocks**. Each block names the skill, passes inputs, and states what it expects back.\n121\t\n122\tThe runtime translates each invoke block into a sub-agent call:\n123\t1. \"Read and follow `agents/<skill-name>/SKILL.md`.\"\n124\t2. Inputs from the invoke block, with actual values substituted.\n125\t\n126\t**Contract validation is mandatory.** For every invoke:\n127\t- Validate invoke input JSON against `agents/<skill>/contract.json` with `--mode inputs`\n128\t- Validate sub-agent return JSON against `agents/<skill>/contract.json` with `--mode returns`\n129\t- If validation fails, stop that step and print `[step] FAILED \u2014 contract validation error`\n130\t\n131\tExample:\n132\t\n133\t```bash\n134\tgo run ./cmd/contract-validate <log_flags> --contract agents/rule-writer/contract.json --mode inputs --payload-file <migration_dir>/contracts/rule-writer-input-1.json\n135\tgo run ./cmd/contract-validate <log_flags> --contract agents/rule-writer/contract.json --mode returns --payload-file <migration_dir>/contracts/rule-writer-return-1.json\n136\t```\n137\t\n138\tIf the runtime supports parallel sub-agents, invoke blocks marked `Parallel: yes` should be dispatched concurrently. If the runtime does not support parallel dispatch or sub-agents, run all invoke blocks sequentially in the current agent context \u2014 read and follow each sub-skill's SKILL.md inline.\n139\t\n140\t**Parallel extraction:** The guide is split into chunks by section, and multiple rule-writer agents process chunks concurrently. The orchestrator merges the partial patterns files and runs construct/validate once. Each agent reads only its assigned sections from the guide.\n141\t\n142\t**Do NOT read sub-agent references.** The orchestrator must NOT read files under `agents/<skill>/references/` \u2014 sub-agents read their own references. The orchestrator only needs to know the invoke contract (inputs/returns). Reading references wastes context and risks the orchestrator overriding sub-agent decisions with its own interpretation of reference material.\n143\t\n144\t**Do NOT micro-manage sub-agent work.** Pass the inputs specified in the invoke block. Do not pre-digest rule YAML, pre-read the guide, or compose line-by-line instructions. The sub-agent's SKILL.md tells it what to read and how to work.\n145\t",

### General

Please read the general [Migration Guide page](migration.html) first, for common considerations that apply to migration or upgrade between versions of Apache Tomcat®.

### Migrating from 9.0.x to 10.0.x

This section lists all the known changes between 9.0.x and 10.0.x which may cause backwards compatibility problems when upgrading.

#### Java 8 required

Apache Tomcat 10.0.x requires Java 8 or later. This is unchanged from Tomcat 9.0.x.

#### Specification APIs

Apache Tomcat 10 supports the Jakarta Servlet 5.0, Jakarta Pages 3.0, Jakarta Expression Language 4.0, JakartaWebSocket 2.0 and Jakarta Authentication 2.0 [specifications](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/TOMCAT/Specifications).

There is a significant breaking change between Tomcat 9.0.x and Tomcat 10.0.x. The Java package used by the specification APIs has changed from javax... to jakarta.... It will be necessary to recompile web applications against the new APIs.

Tomcat can convert an existing web application from Java EE 8 to Jakarta EE 9 at deployment time using the Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE. To make use of the feature, the web application should be placed in the Host `legacyAppBase` folder (by default named `webapps-javaee`) and they will be converted to an equivalent Jakarta EE web application in the Host `appBase` folder (by default named `webapps`).

Alternately, the [Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE](https://tomcat.apache.org/download-migration.cgi) or any similar conversion tool can be used ahead of time to benefit from faster deployment time and more precise conversion configuration options.

#### Servlet 5.0 API

The Java package has changed from javax.servlet to jakarta.servlet.

#### Pages 3.0

The Java package has changed from javax.servlet.jsp to jakarta.servlet.jsp.

#### Expression Language 4.0

The Java package has changed from javax.el to jakarta.el.

#### WebSocket 2.0

The Java package has changed from javax.websocket to jakarta.websocket.

#### Authentication 2.0

The Java package has changed from javax.security.auth.message to jakarta.security.auth.message.

#### Internal APIs

Whilst the Tomcat 10 internal API is broadly compatible with Tomcat 9 there have been many changes at the detail level and they are not binary compatible. Developers of custom components that interact with Tomcat's internals should review the JavaDoc for the relevant API.

Of particular note are:

- GenericPrincipal.getPassword() has been removed.

#### System properties

Support for many of the Tomcat specific system properties has been removed and the system property replaced with an attribute on the appropriate component such as the Connector, Context or Manager.

#### web.xml defaults

`conf/web.xml` sets the default request and response character encoding to UTF-8.

#### Session management

Session persistence on restart has been disabled by default. It may be re-enabled globally in conf/context.xml or per web application.

#### HTTP/2

The configuration settings that were duplicated between the HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 connectors have been removed from the HTTP/2 connector which will now inherit them from the associated HTTP/1.1 connector.

#### Logging

The logging implementation now only creates log files once there is something to write to the log files.

#### Access Log Patterns

To align with httpd, the `%D` pattern now logs request time in microseconds rather than milliseconds. To log request time in milliseconds, use `%{ms}T`.

### Upgrading 10.0.x

When upgrading instances of Apache Tomcat from one version of Tomcat 10 to another, particularly when using separate locations for $CATALINA\_HOME and $CATALINA\_BASE, it is necessary to ensure that any changes in the configuration files such as new attributes and changes to defaults are applied as part of the upgrade. To assist with the identification of these changes, the form below may be used to view the differences between the configuration files in different versions of Tomcat 10.

#### Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes

The Tomcat developers aim for each patch release to be fully backwards compatible with the previous release. Occasionally, it is necessary to break backwards compatibility in order to fix a bug. In most cases, these changes will go unnoticed. This section lists changes that are not fully backwards compatible and might cause breakage when upgrading.

- In 10.0.3 onwards, the semantics of the `HostConfig.check(String)` method have changed. Rather than marking the application as serviced before calling the method, the method will mark the application as serviced before checking resources and then un-mark the application as being serviced after the checks are complete. If the application is marked as serviced when the method is called, the method will be a NO-OP.
- In 10.0.9 onwards, Tomcat no longer adds an "Expires" HTTP response header when adding "Cache-Control: private" due to a CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee. This will likely cause a change in caching behavior for applications that do not explicitly set their own headers but rely on Tomcat's previous behavior. If you wish to disable caching, you will need to configure it explicitly in your application. See [BZ 65513](https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=65513) for more information.
- In 10.0.11 onwards, as a result of the updated fork of Commons FileUpload now using `java.nio.file.Files`, applications using multi-part uploads need to ensure that the JVM is configured with sufficient direct memory to store all in progress multi-part uploads.
- In 10.0.14 onwards, the system property `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval` is no longer used.

#### Tomcat 10.0.x configuration file differences

Select a configuration file, old version and new version from the boxes below and then click "View differences" to see the differences. The differences will be shown in a new tab/window.

**Note:** If there are no differences you will see an error page.

Configuration file: All configuration files catalina.policy catalina.properties context.xml logging.properties server.xml tomcat-users.xml web.xml

Old version: 10.0.0-M1 10.0.0-M3 10.0.0-M4 10.0.0-M5 10.0.0-M6 10.0.0-M7 10.0.0-M8 10.0.0-M9 10.0.0-M10 10.0.0 10.0.2 10.0.4 10.0.5 10.0.6 10.0.7 10.0.8 10.0.10 10.0.11 10.0.12 10.0.13 10.0.14 10.0.16 10.0.17 10.0.18 10.0.20 10.0.21 10.0.22 10.0.23 10.0.26 10.0.27 , new version: 10.0.0-M1 10.0.0-M3 10.0.0-M4 10.0.0-M5 10.0.0-M6 10.0.0-M7 10.0.0-M8 10.0.0-M9 10.0.0-M10 10.0.0 10.0.2 10.0.4 10.0.5 10.0.6 10.0.7 10.0.8 10.0.10 10.0.11 10.0.12 10.0.13 10.0.14 10.0.16 10.0.17 10.0.18 10.0.20 10.0.21 10.0.22 10.0.23 10.0.26 10.0.27 trunk (unreleased)

View Differences

You can also use a Git command similar to the following from within a working copy:

```
git diff 10.0.0 10.0.12 -- conf/
```

  description: javax.servlet.jsp package renamed to jakarta.servlet.jsp in Tomcat 10

  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9

    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Jakarta Server Pages (JSP) API package has changed from `javax.servlet.jsp` to `jakarta.servlet.jsp` in Tomcat 10 (Pages 3.0). All imports and type references using `javax.servlet.jsp` must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import javax.servlet.jsp.JspException;
    import javax.servlet.jsp.tagext.SimpleTagSupport;

    public class MyTag extends SimpleTagSupport {
        @Override
        public void doTag() throws JspException {
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import jakarta.servlet.jsp.JspException;
    import jakarta.servlet.jsp.tagext.SimpleTagSupport;

    public class MyTag extends SimpleTagSupport {
        @Override
        public void doTag() throws JspException {
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All classes under `javax.servlet.jsp` and its subpackages (e.g., `javax.servlet.jsp.tagext`, `javax.servlet.jsp.el`) must be migrated to `jakarta.servlet.jsp`
    - Custom tag libraries and JSP tag handlers need to be updated
    - Web applications must be recompiled against the new Jakarta Pages 3.0 API
    - The Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE can automate this conversion

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/logging.yaml
- ruleID: logging-pattern-00010
  description: Access log %D pattern now logs microseconds instead of milliseconds
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10, the `%D` access log pattern now logs request time in microseconds instead of milliseconds, aligning with httpd behavior.

    ### Before

    ```xml
    <Valve className="org.apache.catalina.valves.AccessLogValve"
           pattern="%h %l %u %t &quot;%r&quot; %s %b %D" />
    ```

    ### After

    ```xml
    <!-- Use %{ms}T for milliseconds -->
    <Valve className="org.apache.catalina.valves.AccessLogValve"
           pattern="%h %l %u %t &quot;%r&quot; %s %b %{ms}T" />
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - If you have monitoring or log analysis tools that parse access log `%D` values as milliseconds, they will now receive microsecond values (1000x larger).
    - To maintain millisecond logging, replace `%D` with `%{ms}T` in your access log pattern.
    - This change aligns Tomcat's access log behavior with Apache httpd.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Access_Log_Patterns
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Access_Log_Patterns
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: '%D'
        filePattern: .*server\.xml
- ruleID: logging-pattern-00020
  description: System property org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval removed in Tomcat 10.0.14
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The system property `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval` is no longer used as of Tomcat 10.0.14.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Search your startup scripts, catalina.properties, and JVM configuration for references to `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval`.
    2. Remove any `-Dorg.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval=...` JVM arguments.
    3. Remove any references to this property from `catalina.properties` or other configuration files.

    ### Additional Info

    - This property was used to configure the poll interval for the async logger in Tomcat's JULI logging implementation.
    - Setting this property in Tomcat 10.0.14+ will have no effect.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: org\.apache\.juli\.AsyncLoggerPollInterval
        filePattern: .*\.(sh|bat|cmd|conf|properties|ya?ml|xml|env|args|Dockerfile)

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/security.yaml
- ruleID: security-import-00010
  description: javax.security.auth.message package renamed to jakarta.security.auth.message in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Java Authentication SPI for Containers (JASPIC) API package has changed from `javax.security.auth.message` to `jakarta.security.auth.message` in Tomcat 10 (Authentication 2.0). All imports and type references using `javax.security.auth.message` must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import javax.security.auth.message.AuthException;
    import javax.security.auth.message.MessageInfo;
    import javax.security.auth.message.module.ServerAuthModule;

    public class MyAuthModule implements ServerAuthModule {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.AuthException;
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.MessageInfo;
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.module.ServerAuthModule;

    public class MyAuthModule implements ServerAuthModule {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All classes under `javax.security.auth.message` and its subpackages (e.g., `javax.security.auth.message.callback`, `javax.security.auth.message.config`, `javax.security.auth.message.module`) must be migrated to `jakarta.security.auth.message`
    - Custom authentication modules (ServerAuthModule implementations) need to be updated
    - Web applications must be recompiled against the new Jakarta Authentication 2.0 API
    - The Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE can automate this conversion
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Authentication_2.0
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.security.auth.message*
        location: PACKAGE
- ruleID: security-method-00010
  description: GenericPrincipal.getPassword() removed in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `GenericPrincipal.getPassword()` method has been removed in Tomcat 10.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review all calls to `GenericPrincipal.getPassword()` in custom Realm implementations or security components.
    2. Replace with an alternative approach — Tomcat 10 no longer exposes the password through the `GenericPrincipal` API.
    3. If you need password verification, use the Realm's `authenticate()` method instead.

    ### Additional Info

    - This change affects custom components that interact with Tomcat's internal security APIs.
    - The `GenericPrincipal` class itself still exists, but the `getPassword()` accessor has been removed.
    - Review the Tomcat 10 JavaDoc for `GenericPrincipal` for available methods.
    - Applications using standard Servlet security APIs are not affected.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Internal_APIs
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Internal_APIs
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.catalina.realm.GenericPrincipal.getPassword
        location: METHOD_CALL
- ruleID: security-pattern-00010
  description: Tomcat no longer adds Expires header with CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10.0.9 onwards, Tomcat no longer adds an `Expires` HTTP response header when adding `Cache-Control: private` due to a `CONFIDENTIAL` transport-guarantee. This may cause a change in caching behavior for applications that do not explicitly set their own headers but relied on Tomcat's previous behavior.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review your `web.xml` for `<transport-guarantee>CONFIDENTIAL</transport-guarantee>` elements.
    2. If your application relied on Tomcat automatically adding `Expires` headers for CONFIDENTIAL resources, you will need to configure caching explicitly in your application.
    3. Add appropriate `Cache-Control` and `Expires` headers in your application code or via a filter.

    ### Additional Info

    - This change affects applications that rely on Tomcat's automatic cache-control behavior for CONFIDENTIAL resources.
    - Applications that explicitly set their own caching headers are not affected.
    - See: https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=65513
  links:
    - url: https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=65513
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: <transport-guarantee>\s*CONFIDENTIAL
        filePattern: .*web\.xml

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-111413/rules/servlet.yaml
- ruleID: servlet-import-00010
  description: javax.servlet package renamed to jakarta.servlet in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Java Servlet API package has changed from `javax.servlet` to `jakarta.servlet` in Tomcat 10 (Servlet 5.0). All imports, type references, and annotations using `javax.servlet` must be updated to use `jakarta.servlet`.

    This is part of the broader Java EE to Jakarta EE transition. Web applications must be recompiled against the new Jakarta Servlet 5.0 API.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import javax.servlet.http.HttpServlet;
    import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
    import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

    public class MyServlet extends HttpServlet {
        @Override
        protected void doGet(HttpServletRequest req, HttpServletResponse resp) {
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServlet;
    import jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
    import jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

    public class MyServlet extends HttpServlet {
        @Override
        protected void doGet(HttpServletRequest req, HttpServletResponse resp) {
            // ...
        }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All classes under `javax.servlet` and its subpackages (e.g., `javax.servlet.http`, `javax.servlet.annotation`) must be migrated to `jakarta.servlet`
    - Tomcat provides a migration tool that can convert web applications from Java EE 8 to Jakarta EE 9 at deployment time by placing them in the `webapps-javaee` directory
    - The [Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE](https://tomcat.apache.org/download-migration.cgi) can also be used ahead of time for faster deployment
    - This change requires recompilation of all web application code
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Servlet_5.0_API
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.servlet*
        location: PACKAGE
- ruleID: servlet-annotation-00010
  description: Multi-part uploads now use java.nio.file.Files requiring sufficient JVM direct memory
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10.0.11 onwards, the updated fork of Commons FileUpload now uses `java.nio.file.Files` for multi-part uploads. Applications using multi-part uploads need to ensure that the JVM is configured with sufficient direct memory (`-XX:MaxDirectMemorySize`) to store all in-progress multi-part uploads.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Identify all servlets annotated with `@MultipartConfig` (which becomes `@jakarta.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig` after the javax-to-jakarta migration).
    2. Estimate the maximum concurrent upload size for your application.
    3. Configure the JVM with sufficient direct memory by adding `-XX:MaxDirectMemorySize=<size>` to your JVM startup arguments (e.g., in `setenv.sh` or `setenv.bat`).
    4. If you set `maxFileSize` or `maxRequestSize` in your `@MultipartConfig` annotation, use those values to guide the direct memory sizing.

    ### Additional Info

    - The default JVM direct memory size may not be sufficient for applications handling large or many concurrent file uploads.
    - This change is due to Commons FileUpload internally switching from heap-based I/O to `java.nio.file.Files`, which uses direct memory buffers.
    - If direct memory is exhausted, uploads will fail with `OutOfMemoryError: Direct buffer memory`.
    - Consider setting `-XX:MaxDirectMemorySize` to at least the sum of all expected concurrent upload sizes.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig
        location: ANNOTATION

- ruleID: session-import-00010
  description: Session persistence on restart disabled by default in Tomcat 10
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Session persistence on restart has been disabled by default in Tomcat 10. In Tomcat 9, sessions were persisted across restarts by default.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. If your application relies on session persistence across Tomcat restarts, re-enable it in `conf/context.xml` or your application's `META-INF/context.xml`.
    2. Add `<Manager pathname="SESSIONS.ser" />` to your Context configuration to re-enable session persistence.
    3. If your application does not rely on session persistence across restarts, no changes are needed.

    ### Additional Info

    - This change affects all web applications running on the Tomcat instance.
    - Session persistence can be re-enabled globally in `conf/context.xml` or per web application in `META-INF/context.xml`.
    - Applications that programmatically interact with the `StandardManager` API should review their session management code.
    - See: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Session_management
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Session_management
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:

        pattern: org.apache.catalina.session.StandardManager
        location: IMPORT

- ruleID: websocket-import-00010
  description: javax.websocket package renamed to jakarta.websocket in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The WebSocket API package has changed from `javax.websocket` to `jakarta.websocket` in Tomcat 10 (WebSocket 2.0). All imports and type references using `javax.websocket` must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import javax.websocket.OnMessage;
    import javax.websocket.Session;
    import javax.websocket.server.ServerEndpoint;

    @ServerEndpoint("/ws")
    public class MyWebSocket {
        @OnMessage
        public String onMessage(String message, Session session) {
            return "Echo: " + message;
        }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import jakarta.websocket.OnMessage;
    import jakarta.websocket.Session;
    import jakarta.websocket.server.ServerEndpoint;

    @ServerEndpoint("/ws")
    public class MyWebSocket {
        @OnMessage
        public String onMessage(String message, Session session) {
            return "Echo: " + message;
        }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All classes under `javax.websocket` and its subpackages (e.g., `javax.websocket.server`) must be migrated to `jakarta.websocket`
    - WebSocket endpoints, decoders, encoders, and client APIs all need to be updated
    - Web applications must be recompiled against the new Jakarta WebSocket 2.0 API
    - The Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE can automate this conversion
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#WebSocket_2.0
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.websocket*
        location: PACKAGE
case-005-junit4-to-junit5 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $7.54 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The patterns.json captures the vast majority of migration artifacts from the guide. All annotation renames are covered (@Test, @Before/@BeforeEach, @After/@AfterEach, @BeforeClass/@BeforeAll, @AfterClass/@AfterAll, @Ignore/@Disabled). The @RunWith→@ExtendWith, @Category→@Tag, @Rule/@ClassRule removal, TestRule→extension interfaces, Assert→Assertions, Assume→Assumptions, SpringJUnit4ClassRunner→SpringExtension, Parameterized→@ParameterizedTest, and the junit:junit dependency are all captured. Minor omissions include: (1) The @Test(expected=...) → assertThrows() and @Test(timeout=...) → assertTimeout() behavioral changes are mentioned in messages but not as separate dedicated patterns with their own source_fqn targeting the specific attribute usage; (2) The JUnit Vintage Engine dependency (junit-vintage-engine) mentioned in section 3.7 is not captured as a separate pattern — it's only referenced in the dependency migration message; (3) The assertAll() grouped assertions feature from section 3.2 and assumingThat() from section 3.3 are new JUnit 5 features mentioned in messages but don't need separate source patterns since they're additions not migrations; (4) The maven-surefire-plugin configuration change (includeTags/excludeTags) from section 3.4 is not captured as a separate pattern. Overall coverage is strong at roughly 90%, with the omissions being mostly secondary/contextual items rather than primary migration artifacts.

patterns_qualityPASS

16 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 16 rules, 93.75% pass rate

rule_correctness5

All sampled rules have accurate source-side when conditions with correct location types (ANNOTATION, IMPORT, IMPLEMENTS_TYPE). Every rule includes clear before/after code examples, explains what changed and how to migrate, and references specific documentation sections. All source FQNs are verified real artifacts from JUnit 4.13.2 and Spring Test. Category (mandatory) and effort values are well-calibrated to complexity. The single test failure (dependencies-dependency-00010) is a kantra test infrastructure issue (missing Eclipse project files), not a rule defect. No hallucinated classes or methods were found in any rule.

import org.junit.Rule;

import org.junit.runners.model.Statement;

public class ApplicationTest {

    // Rule: rules-annotation-00020
    @ClassRule
    public static ExternalResource classResource = new ExternalResource() {
        @Override
        protected void before() throws Throwable {
        }

        @Override
        protected void after() {
        }
    };

    // Rule: rules-annotation-00010
    @Rule
    public TestRule instanceRule = new TestRule() {
        @Override
        public Statement apply(Statement base, Description description) {
            return base;
        }
    };
}

// Rule: rules-type-00010
class CustomTestRule implements TestRule {
    @Override
    public Statement apply(Statement base, Description description) {
        return base;
    }
}

output/junit4-to-junit5-20260624-111419/rules/annotations.yaml
- ruleID: annotations-import-00010
  description: JUnit 4 Parameterized runner replaced by JUnit 5 @ParameterizedTest
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The JUnit 4 `@RunWith(Parameterized.class)` approach for parameterized tests has been replaced by the `@ParameterizedTest` annotation in JUnit 5. JUnit 5 provides a more flexible and intuitive approach to parameterized tests with dedicated source annotations.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import org.junit.Test;
    import org.junit.runner.RunWith;
    import org.junit.runners.Parameterized;
    import org.junit.runners.Parameterized.Parameters;

    @RunWith(Parameterized.class)
    public class MyParameterizedTest {
        @Parameters
        public static Collection<Object[]> data() {
            return Arrays.asList(new Object[][] { {1, 2}, {3, 4} });
        }

        @Test
        public void testAddition() { /* ... */ }
    }
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.params.ParameterizedTest;
    import org.junit.jupiter.params.provider.CsvSource;

    class MyParameterizedTest {
        @ParameterizedTest
        @CsvSource({"1, 2", "3, 4"})
        void testAddition(int a, int b) { /* ... */ }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - JUnit 5 supports multiple parameter sources: `@ValueSource`, `@CsvSource`, `@MethodSource`, `@EnumSource`, and `@ArgumentsSource`
    - The `@ParameterizedTest` annotation replaces both `@RunWith(Parameterized.class)` and `@Test`
    - Parameters are injected directly into test method arguments instead of through constructor or field injection
    - Add `org.junit.jupiter:junit-jupiter-params` dependency for parameterized test support
    - See the [JUnit 5 Parameterized Tests Guide](https://junit.org/junit5/docs/current/user-guide/#writing-tests-parameterized-tests) for complete documentation
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.junit.runners.Parameterized
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: annotations-import-00020
  description: SpringJUnit4ClassRunner replaced by SpringExtension for JUnit 5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `SpringJUnit4ClassRunner` (used with `@RunWith` in JUnit 4) is replaced by `SpringExtension` (used with `@ExtendWith` in JUnit 5) for Spring test integration. JUnit 5 uses the extension model instead of runners.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import org.junit.runner.RunWith;
    import org.springframework.test.context.junit4.SpringJUnit4ClassRunner;
    import org.springframework.test.context.ContextConfiguration;

    @RunWith(SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.class)
    @ContextConfiguration({"app-config.xml"})
    public class MySpringTest {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.extension.ExtendWith;
    import org.springframework.test.context.junit.jupiter.SpringExtension;
    import org.springframework.test.context.ContextConfiguration;

    @ExtendWith(SpringExtension.class)
    @ContextConfiguration({"app-config.xml"})
    class MySpringTest {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - In Spring Boot 2.1+, `@SpringBootTest` already includes `@ExtendWith(SpringExtension.class)`, so explicit declaration is not needed
    - `SpringRunner` (a shorthand for `SpringJUnit4ClassRunner`) should also be migrated to `SpringExtension`
    - The `@ExtendWith` annotation can be combined with other extensions, unlike `@RunWith` which only supported one runner
    - Consider using `@SpringBootTest` instead of manual `@ExtendWith(SpringExtension.class)` + `@ContextConfiguration` where appropriate
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.test.context.junit4.SpringJUnit4ClassRunner
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: annotations-annotation-00010
  description: '@Test annotation moved from org.junit to org.junit.jupiter.api in JUnit 5'
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `@Test` annotation has moved from `org.junit.Test` to `org.junit.jupiter.api.Test` in JUnit 5. Additionally, the `expected` and `timeout` parameters of `@Test` have been removed. Use `Assertions.assertThrows()` for expected exceptions and `Assertions.assertTimeout()` for timeout assertions.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Test;

    @Test(expected = Exception.class)
    public void shouldRaiseAnException() throws Exception {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions;

    @Test
    void shouldRaiseAnException() {
        Assertions.assertThrows(Exception.class, () -> {
            // ...
        });
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `expected` parameter is replaced by `Assertions.assertThrows()` which returns the thrown exception for further assertions
    - The `timeout` parameter is replaced by `Assertions.assertTimeout()` which accepts a `Duration` parameter
    - Test methods no longer need to be `public` in JUnit 5
    - The `@Test` annotation no longer supports any parameters
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.junit.Test
        location: ANNOTATION
- ruleID: annotations-annotation-00020
  description: '@Before annotation renamed to @BeforeEach in JUnit 5'
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `@Before` annotation has been renamed to `@BeforeEach` in JUnit 5. Update all usages of `@org.junit.Before` to `@org.junit.jupiter.api.BeforeEach`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Before;

    @Before
    public void setUp() {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.BeforeEach;

    @BeforeEach
    void setUp() {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The method no longer needs to be `public`
    - Semantically identical to `@Before` -- runs before each test method
    - Part of the `org.junit.jupiter.api` package
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation

        pattern: org.junit.Before
